Current Commentary 10

The Future of the War

(1) The Invocation of Article 16 of the League of Nations Covenant

Since trampling on Manchuria and creating a puppet state, Japanese militarists have, under the guise of a special relationship, deliberately provoked challenges. Their actions are not merely aimed at monopolizing the economic markets of the Far East. Therefore, the Nineteen-Member Committee can no longer tolerate and allow Japan to tear up all international conventions and disregard [good faith] to dominate the world with military force. Although the draft resolution submitted by the Nineteen-Member Committee may not be adopted as originally proposed, the violent aggression of Japanese imperialism has since been recognized by the whole world. Our country, as the victim, if it can promptly strive for self-rescue, then the sanctions of Article 16 of the League of Nations Covenant—economic blockade against Japan—will not be difficult to realize.

Enlightened people in that country have long harbored a sense of caution. Even the boastful Osaka Asahi Shimbun understands that Japan is trapped in diplomatic isolation and that it is foolish to turn [the entire country into ruins]. Therefore, it advocates [avoiding] [war] and handling matters with caution. However, we have observed that in the past year and a half, Japanese public opinion has been completely dominated by militarist ideology. Consider the non-official opinion expressed by the Japanese Navy Department on February 22: [Withdrawal from the League of Nations is a foreseeable fact. … If anyone dares to impose an economic blockade, … our (Japan) navy is prepared to punish them with force. …]

[… The mandated administration of the South Pacific islands. Anyone who dares to deny the solemn sovereignty of (Japan) empire will be resolutely repelled. We will stake our lives to ensure that the South Pacific islands (Japan) maritime lifeline does not leave Japan's hands [… The Rehe issue is an internal matter of Manchukuo. …]

Such a statement is not only absurd but also a direct challenge to the world. Whether the League of Nations will reluctantly endure it or, failing to do so, issue a protest, it is unlikely to receive a satisfactory and reasonable response from Japan. However, our country, at this critical juncture, must not seek temporary comfort and must not rely on the assistance of foreign powers. In the face of the enemy's invasion, how can we rely on past treaties as the basis for reasoning?

The situation has reached this point. First, we must launch a complete national struggle, risking the blood of 400 million people to fight the brutal enemy. Second, Rehe is the shield and key to the northern gate of Pingjin, which needs no detailed discussion. Today, the enemy wants to use a puppet regime to rely on Rehe to gradually encroach on North China. For the sake of the country's future, the nation's survival, and the future recovery of the lost territories of the three northeastern provinces, we should devote the strength of the entire nation to defending Rehe. We should resolutely and fiercely strike back when the enemy comes to attack. We should also do our utmost to pursue the retreating enemy and recover our former territories. Third, in resisting, we are in a passive position. If the enemy does not attack, we are in a state of decline. In the future, we must reverse the situation, take advantage of the national resurgence, turn resistance into counter-offensive, and launch a war to recover the lost territories of the Northeast. We must officially send troops to punish the puppet state and initiate a prelude to war to punish the brutal actions of Japanese imperialism with force. (2) War of Self-Defense

After the draft resolution of the League of Nations Nineteen-Member Committee was submitted, the world has jointly recognized that the actions of the Japanese army in Manchuria are aggression. However, the Japanese army continues its aggression unabated. Although we have already achieved a [moral victory], if there is no strength to back it up, it will ultimately be in vain. Moreover, the justice of the international community must be based on the strength of the parties. Therefore, at this point, [reasoning] has come to an end. We should change our approach and stand up to fight with military force. Our country's weakness is not of one day's making. The enemy is emboldened to bully us because they believe we dare not speak of war. They are using threatening tactics everywhere, using a small number of troops to achieve maximum effect. If we were to fight with all our might, the crises lurking within Japan would also erupt one by one. We are forced to launch a [war] for self-defense. Domestically, it is enough to eliminate all our own contradictions, invigorate the declining spirit, unite disparate actions, make great sacrifices, and reverse the decline of our nation. Externally, other countries will see the results of our determined struggle and be able to abandon their previous contemptuous views, listen to the [justice] we advocate, and recover the lost territories of the Northeast. It is impossible to maintain world peace and justice without us paying a heavy price in iron and blood.

Furthermore, once the war against Japan begins, the entire country will naturally enter a state of war. The situation in the Far East market can also be imagined. The United Kingdom, the United States, the Soviet Union, and France will find it impossible to stand idly by and watch the Sino-Japanese war. It is time to invoke Article 16 of the League of Nations Covenant for sanctions. Therefore, enlightened people in Japan also plan to avoid war. If it breaks out, Article 16 of the Covenant will follow with economic sanctions. Japan will experience the same predicament as Germany during the European War. Although its navy is deliberately making alarming statements to intimidate the powers and coerce our country, its outwardly strong but inwardly weak nature is an open secret. How can it be concealed?

Our country has lost more than 3.8 million square miles of territory. Is avenging this humiliation the same as aggression? Moreover, if we insist on fighting, the power to sanction violence will be in our hands. Inspiring world peace will also depend on whether our country can use iron and blood to shatter the delusion of Japanese militarism.

League of Nations Assembly Reopens Today 11

Chinese and Japanese Representatives to Speak

Report to be Put to Vote Immediately

Japanese Government Instructs Matsuoka to Declare Opposition to League of Nations Recommendations

Special Committee's Continued Existence and Exercise of Authority Deemed Necessary

(Geneva) The Nineteen-Nation Special Committee convened this afternoon and decided on the agenda for tomorrow's General Assembly. First, the chairman will report, followed by representatives from the three small nations and the Chinese representative. Finally, the report will be put to a vote. In addition to deciding on the General Assembly's agenda, the special committee also discussed other difficult issues. All committee members agreed that the special committee's continued existence and exercise of authority are necessary. (Central News Agency dispatch from Geneva, 3:30 AM, 24th)

(Geneva) The League of Nations Assembly is scheduled to consider the report and recommendations of the Nineteen-Nation Special Committee tomorrow. However, its position on the agenda is constantly changing and cannot be determined until the special committee meets today. Those who support the idea of not issuing arguments when the official meeting opens tomorrow are practically numerous. After Hymans' address tomorrow morning, the Chinese and Japanese representatives will speak in succession. Then, this report must be submitted to the League of Nations Political Committee. This procedure was recently invented by those who study formalities. The Political Committee, following the precedent set by the initial sessions of last year's League of Nations Extraordinary Assembly, may not differ much from the League of Nations Assembly itself. In any case, the committee can give those who wish to speak an opportunity to do so. Then, the Political Committee will amend the General Assembly to make a final passage. The impact of this procedure may extend the meeting beyond Friday. (Reuters dispatch, 23rd) (Nanjing) According to diplomatic circles, the League of Nations Assembly will reconvene on the 24th, and the report will be supported by all except Japan. According to the law, the report can take effect without the consent of the countries involved, so Japan's negative vote will be of no avail. The Assembly will not adjourn and will convene when necessary. Whether the special committee will continue to exist or a negotiating committee will be formed quickly will be decided at the Assembly on the 25th. We will raise the issue of Jehol after the report is passed and request effective measures to stop Japan's acts of aggression. (Central News Agency dispatch, 23rd)

(Geneva) The Nineteen-Nation Special Committee, in completing its report on the Sino-Japanese dispute to be submitted to the League of Nations Assembly, believes that its duties have come to an end. However, when it convenes tomorrow, it will see that its responsibilities and difficulties are far from over. During the Special Committee's meeting on Thursday, several difficulties may arise, such as the decision of the League of Nations Assembly's agenda, the completion of the organization of the negotiation committee, the discussion of what actions the League of Nations should take when the Jehol war breaks out, and the resolution of how to maintain the League of Nations Assembly so that it can handle the various developments after the report is passed. All are events that the Special Committee must deal with tomorrow. The Special Committee is currently exercising its judicial functions. It has already drafted its verdict in a secret meeting. Now, following the guidance of Chairman Hymans, it will not only announce the verdict but also accept the various events that occurred during the meeting. Hymans handles various matters in his capacity as chairman, and everyone is convinced and admires him greatly, believing that no one else can lead the committee's work. Chinese Chief Delegate Dr. Yen Hui-ching will speak before the report is passed, and the gist of his speech has already been drafted, but how to phrase it will depend on the extent of satisfaction he obtains when the Special Committee meets tomorrow. After Dr. Yen's speech, several countries that are not members of the Special Committee, such as Canada, may make some statements. However, Japanese Representative Matsuoka will probably speak only after the report is passed. It is estimated that Matsuoka's words will not go beyond the scope of the arguments made by the Japanese delegation yesterday, which are nothing more than refusing to revoke the recognition of ["Manchukuo"], declaring the Jehol incident to be an internal affair of ["Manchukuo"], and pointing out that the League of Nations should bear part of the responsibility for the current situation. The Nineteen-Nation Special Committee has slightly different opinions on how to continue to contact the situation. Some suggest that the League of Nations Assembly should continue to be convened at any time by the League of Nations Secretary-General Drummond. Others advocate the establishment of another body, such as the Nineteen-Nation Special Committee. At the same time, others advocate that the structure of the report should be changed slightly so that the negotiating committee can meet as soon as possible, regardless of whether both parties accept the report. There are quite a few people who agree with the third theory above, because they feel that this method can obtain the cooperation of Russia and the United States in the future situation, which is considered to be the most serious scene since the outbreak of the Sino-Japanese conflict. (Reuters dispatch, 22nd)

Our Country's Representative

Main Points of Assembly Speech

(Geneva) The main points of our country's Representative Yen's speech at tomorrow's League of Nations Assembly, in addition to those already detailed in the previous telegrams, will further clarify and reaffirm China's sovereignty in Manchuria, which is the cornerstone of consolidating international treaties and the League of Nations, and declare that the Chinese government is willing to accept the report and welcomes the participation of the United States and Russia in the negotiations. After Representative Yen's speech, Representative Koo may speak to explain the seriousness of the Jehol situation and ask the League of Nations to find ways to prevent the situation from escalating as soon as possible. (Central News Agency dispatch, 23rd)

Japanese Government's Final Decision

Steps to Deal with the League of Nations

Instructs Matsuoka to Firmly Reject Advice

(Tokyo) The Japanese Foreign Ministry held a leadership meeting today and decided on the final steps for the League of Nations Assembly to reconvene on the 24th. The content of the telegram to the Japanese delegation is as follows: (1) Matsuoka must answer Chairman Hymans' speech on the 24th with an absolutely tough attitude and cannot relax in the slightest. (2) When the report is put to a vote at the Assembly, oppose it with the greatest strength, and finally cast a negative vote and issue a declaration of non-cooperation. (3) Insist on proceeding with Article 15, Paragraph 5, while the delegation withdraws from Geneva and prepares to return home. (4) Finally, explain the reasons why Japan is severing ties with the League of Nations and prepare to formally notify the League of Nations of its withdrawal on March 1. (China United Press dispatch, 23rd)

(Tokyo) The Japanese Cabinet held a cabinet meeting this afternoon at the Prime Minister's official residence. Minister of War Araki reported on the Jehol war situation, and Foreign Minister Uchida proposed three draft instructions: (1) A written statement not accepting the recommendation. (2) Representative Matsuoka's declaration at the Assembly. (3) After the recommendation is established, what form should the proposal to sever ties with the League of Nations take? After careful discussion, the original drafts of the Foreign Ministry were approved. After the cabinet meeting, Foreign Minister Uchida entered the palace to request the Emperor's approval. A telegram was sent to Matsuoka Yosuke tonight, instructing him to act accordingly at tomorrow's Assembly. It is reported that the general outline of the content is as follows: (1) Japan has cooperated with the League of Nations every time in the past thirteen years to maintain world peace, and the League of Nations should pay attention to this point. (2) The international dispute in the Far East is not due to Japan's aggression, but to China's lack of internal governance. To solve the Far East problem, China's internal affairs must be unified. (3) The culture of the three northeastern provinces is different from that of Europe, and European political philosophy cannot be applied. Only by recognizing ["Manchukuo"] can peace in the Far East be maintained. (4) Japan absolutely cannot accept the League of Nations' recommendation. If the League of Nations passes the recommendation, Japan will not be able to cooperate with the League of Nations in the future. (5) Japan cannot be held responsible for any incidents that occur in the world regarding peace after the recommendation is passed. (China United Press dispatch, 23rd)

(Geneva) Representative Matsuoka has decided to leave Geneva for The Hague and London on the 25th, and will cross the Atlantic from England to the United States around March 10th, staying for two or three weeks. He is scheduled to take the Asama Maru and arrive in Yokohama around late April. Representatives Nagaoka and Sato will also leave Geneva on the 25th and 26th. After the 27th, only Information Chief Yokoyama, Sakamoto, and Honno will remain in Geneva to sort out the remaining affairs. (United News dispatch, 23rd)

Japan's Withdrawal from the League of Nations Hesitates and Looks Back 12

(Tokyo) The question of whether Japan will withdraw from the League of Nations is still undecided. However, it is reported that the Japanese Cabinet has decided to order the Japanese delegation in Geneva to retreat to London or Paris to await developments after the League of Nations passes the report of the Nineteen-Nation Special Committee. One thing seems certain: Japan will reject the recommendation and vote against the report. Although there are differing opinions throughout Japan regarding withdrawal from the League of Nations, there is unanimous opposition to the report. According to the Japanese, Japan may have agreed to the recommendation of Manchurian autonomy a year ago, with China retaining sovereignty on the surface. However, there may have been doubts at first whether the recommendation of ["Manchukuo"] could be a satisfactory solution to the Manchurian issue. Since the agreement was concluded last September, these doubts have disappeared, it is said. As for the question of whether Japan will withdraw from the League of Nations, public opinion is clearly divided. Judging from the phenomenon, even if a decision to withdraw is made, it will not be realized until several weeks or several months after the report is passed. The reason for not withdrawing immediately is to avoid the appearance of being driven by a momentary impulse, and to bid farewell to the League of Nations in a friendly spirit. (Reuters dispatch, 23rd)

An Embargo on Arms Should First Determine Who is the Aggressor 13

We are Self-Defensive and Have Not Prepared for War

If an Embargo is Imposed on Both China and Japan Equally

It Would Only Encourage Japan's Belligerence

Britain Does Not Intend to Act Alone and Plans to Cooperate Internationally

(Nanjing) This morning, a Chinese spokesperson commented on the matter of various countries currently discussing a ban on the transportation of arms to countries fighting in the Far East, saying that the Chinese government certainly agrees with the principle of a ban, but this principle cannot be applied to the Sino-Japanese dispute. Japan is currently the aggressor, while China is purely self-defensive. In addition, Japan has already prepared sufficient arms, while China has not prepared for war. If arms exports are banned and implemented equally for both China and Japan, then the powers are no less than assisting Japan's aggression in China. (Reuters dispatch, 23rd) (London) The British government is currently studying the possibility of taking international action to ban the transport of arms to the Far East. This matter is particularly simple in France, Britain, and Italy, requiring only the refusal to issue export passports. However, it is not so easy in the United States and other countries. The Cabinet approved the steps to be taken on the ban issue tonight and put forward suggestions for future actions, but it also resolved that Britain cannot act alone and must act jointly with other arms-exporting countries. During the House of Commons meeting today, former Cabinet member Samuel stated that he would question the government on February 27 as to whether it had consulted with other powers and autonomous regions on imposing a uniform ban on any warring country that the League of Nations condemned for abusing force in supplying it with arms. (Reuters dispatch, 22nd)

(London) Regarding the issue of banning the transport of arms to the Far East, some people asked political figures about the British government's attitude. According to the answer, this matter should be decided by the League of Nations, and it must first determine who is the aggressor. Since the League of Nations has not made any decision on this matter, if the transport of arms is to be banned, it must be carried out simultaneously for both belligerent parties. However, Japan has factories that manufacture arms, while China does not. Under such circumstances, the result of banning the transport of arms will inevitably be contrary to what people generally hope for, and this ban must be carried out unanimously by all countries, and the United States must also agree to it. (Havas dispatch, 22nd)

(London) Today, it was learned that various countries have not yet put forward any concrete proposals regarding banning the transport of arms to China and Japan, and the League of Nations does not have a structure for implementing an arms embargo. However, this embargo can be implemented by member states, and there have been no negotiations on this issue between various countries so far. (Reuters dispatch, 23rd)

Large Quantities of British Arms Exported to the Far East

(London) Regarding the issue of banning the export of arms to the Far East, an important message was published in this morning's newspapers, stating that [the recent export of arms to the Far East is not only enough to encourage the British arms industry but also greatly helps the British shipping industry]. The Daily Guide stated, [Since New Year's Day, a certain British factory has exported 36 million rounds of ammunition to the Far East, and another factory has exported 1,000 machine guns]. It is noted that Britain's total exports for the entire last year were only 13 million rounds of ammunition and 800 machine guns. ] The Daily Express also reported, [Vickers Armstrong factories are working three shifts a day and night to rush-manufacture ammunition for export to the Far East, and recently, not only China and Japan, but also the Siamese government has ordered large quantities of ammunition and machine guns from British factories]. (National Telegram, 23rd)

(London) According to the Liverpool correspondent of the ["Daily Telegraph"], arms destined for China are currently being loaded in Liverpool and other British ports. The exact amount of these arms is kept strictly secret, but it has been learned from official circles that a ship sailing to China yesterday was loaded with explosives. According to well-informed sources, there is no ban on arms exports, and explosives have often been loaded for export for some time, and the number has increased even more recently. Japanese Navy Expresses Determination to be an Enemy of the World 17

To Deal with Economic Sanctions from Various Countries

The Mandated Territory in the South Seas Will Not Be Abandoned

(Tokyo) A spokesman for the Naval Ministry stated that Japan cannot accept the League of Nations' recommendations regarding the Manchurian dispute. From the Japanese perspective, this action shows that Japan does not want to go to war with China. At the same time, there is a saying that the border committee organized by representatives of Japan (["Manchukuo"] and Russia is expected to be realized soon, and the speaker indicates that Japan intends to reduce the danger of conflict with Russia. As for the ban on supplying arms, the general opinion of the Japanese is that this measure is beneficial and harmless, because Japan is a self-sufficient country, and banning the transport of arms will not cause Japan great inconvenience, but will only anger Japan. (Reuters dispatch, 23rd)

Japanese Financial Difficulties

Currency Inflation and a Sharp Decline in Gold Reserves

(Tokyo) In mid-August of last year, banks in various provinces of Japan experienced difficulties, and the financial authorities reduced the loan interest rate from 4.2% to 3% to allow banks in various provinces to borrow at low interest rates to tide over the difficulties. Finance Minister Takahashi believed at the time that savings bureau deposits would increase by 200 million yen by the end of December last year. Unexpectedly, from August to the present, savings bureau deposits have decreased by more than 200 million yen. The difference between the two numbers has reached 400 million yen. As a result, the financial authorities felt great difficulty. In order to reduce unemployment, the Japanese government originally planned to spend approximately 226 million yen on various projects. However, after the savings bureau's deposits decreased, these huge sums of money could not be raised, and some of the valuable securities stored in the savings bureau had to be sold. Japan had to issue approximately 100 million yen in convertible notes to compensate for the budget deficit in 1933-34. The issuance of these convertible notes will inevitably cause currency inflation. The Japanese authorities are now working hard to prevent currency inflation, or at least to reduce it. If the savings bureau sells some of its valuable securities, then the authorities' efforts will be even more difficult. (Havas dispatch, 20th)

Li Liejun Discusses National Defense 20

(Nanjing) Li Liejun said that the purpose of his visit to Nanjing was to support the central government's active resistance against Japan and to hope to reform internal affairs so that the military and civilians could unite and rise up, and use their full strength to revitalize the country. Therefore, he submitted a letter of opinion as soon as he arrived in Nanjing, which has been carefully discussed. Regarding the national defense plan, most of the items are things that the responsible authorities originally planned to do, and are generally the same, and are already being actively planned and implemented. If they can be put into practice, then it will not be difficult to save the country and revitalize the country. It is still waiting for the Central Political Committee to discuss it in detail, or a resolution can be reached. As for resisting insults, some people in the country are quite worried that their weapons are not as good as those of enemy countries. In fact, the victory or defeat of a war depends first on national spirit and right and wrong. The reason why countries all over the world are now jointly sanctioning Japan is that they are wrong and we are right. The reason why the 19th Route Army and the 5th Army and other armies were able to crush the strong enemy in the Battle of Shanghai was because of the national spirit. Chairman Chiang is currently suppressing bandits at the front and will soon return to Nanjing to preside over the meeting. Chairman Feng will also arrive in Nanjing soon to discuss major plans together. The central government is becoming more consolidated, and the intelligence of the people can gradually be expected to be realized. I will go to Shanghai in a few days to pack up my family affairs and then come to Nanjing again. (Special Telegram, 23rd)

The Central Government Has a Whole Plan to Deal with the Current Situation 21

(Nanjing) Since the report of the Nineteen-Nation Committee was published, Japan has actually threatened to withdraw from the League of Nations, and at the same time intimidated us by blockading our seaports. On the one hand, it is actively preparing for a general offensive on Jehol. According to a telegram on the 23rd, the Jehol War officially began on the 20th, and a major war is about to break out. If the Japanese bandits are barbaric and disregard world peace, and actually implement a blockade of our seaports, what strategy should our country adopt? A certain military expert said that the central government has already planned this matter thoroughly. If China and Japan declare war, Japan will use its superior navy to blockade our seaports and cut off our supplies. However, the result will inevitably lead to the intervention of the powers and repeat the tragedy of the Second World War. In my observation, as a result of the war, Japan will become the post-war Germany, which is the best opportunity for our country to rise. Some people suspect that our country will become the Belgium of the war. This is really an overestimation of the current international situation. As for the steps and strategies that our country will take, the central government has a whole plan, which concerns military secrets and cannot be told. (Special Telegram, 23rd)

Peiping Post Office Detains Illegal Mail 22

(Peiping) The Peiping Post Office recently discovered that the communication office of fellow villagers from the three northeastern provinces was packing letters sent back to their hometowns by people from the Northeast into large mailbags and sending them to a certain place in Yuguan for forwarding out of customs. The bureau considered that the place violated the postal regulations and contradicted the government's order to suspend the mailing of mail from the Northeast. In addition to detaining more than 130 of these letters, it also reported to the authorities to strictly investigate and deal with the matter. (Special Telegram, 23rd)

Sun Ke's Telegram Reply to Various Circles in Jehol 23

And a Telegram to the Generals at the Front

(Nanjing) Legislative Yuan President Sun Ke sent a telegram on the 23rd to various circles in Jehol and Zhang Xueliang, etc., expressing his willingness to encourage the people and act as a backing. The original telegrams are as follows: (1) To all sectors of agriculture, industry, commerce, and education, and all the people of Jehol: Having respectfully read your telegram, we understand your feelings. The violent Japanese are greedy and insatiable. Having already obtained Liaodong, they now covet Jehol. Is there any place that is not our territory, yet they are allowed to trample upon it? Is there any one who is not our citizen, yet they are allowed to be slaughtered? Now, the central government has made a firm resolution, and the generals deeply understand the great cause, their spirit is strong and martial, and victory lies in harmony. To pull us out of the fire and water and restore our rivers and mountains depends on this one action. As long as our elders and brothers cry out, how dare we not encourage the people and act as a backing? I hereby reply to your telegram. Do not let your hearts hang in suspense. Sun Ke, President of the Legislative Yuan, with seal. (2) To Acting Chairman Zhang of the Beiping Military Affairs Commission, and to the generals at the front: Having respectfully read your telegram, we understand your situation. Japan has been plotting against us with all its national strength for many years. They have abandoned faith and betrayed their neighbors, and indulged in cruelty to the people. They disregard justice and only rely on power. Like a fire burning the prairie, they cannot be approached. The generals feel the danger of being in a collapsing house and the pain of biting their own navels. They vow to lead the three armies and fight them to the end. It is said, "Victory lies in harmony, one strike exhausts the energy." It is an ancient teaching to clarify shame and teach war in order to kill the enemy. If evil is prolonged, it will eventually reach its end. Those who hold the winning calculation will eventually belong to us. Looking north at the clouds on the border, we await the good news of victory. Sun Ke, President of the Legislative Yuan, with seal. (23rd, Central News Agency dispatch)

The Military Authorities in Beiping Have Not Received

The So-Called Final Ultimatum

(Beiping) It is generally believed here that the so-called Japanese side will present a final ultimatum is entirely a formality, because the ultimatum has not yet been presented, and the war has already broken out. It is said that the ultimatum could have been delivered this afternoon, but it has not been received so far. Tonight, the Chinese authorities declared that they have not yet seen the so-called "ultimatum," and even Japanese officials said they knew nothing about it. (22nd, Reuters dispatch)

(Beiping) The Japanese side is spreading propaganda that the puppet organization will deliver a so-called final ultimatum to us, demanding the withdrawal of troops stationed in Jehol Province within a time limit, otherwise it will be resolved by force. According to official sources, as of noon today, no documents have been received from any puppet organization. Even if they were received, they would be ignored. (23rd, special dispatch)

(Beiping) According to Japanese sources, the ultimatum that Japan is about to present will likely only be presented orally in Nanjing, which is already sufficient and does not need to be presented in Beiping again, because Zhang Xueliang has repeatedly stated that his actions are in accordance with the instructions of the central government. (23rd, Reuters dispatch)

Japanese Residents in Tianjin Organize a Volunteer Corps

Security in the Japanese Concession is Tightened

(Tianjin) The Japanese military authorities officially announced on the 23rd that because the 1,500 stationed troops are insufficient, they have decided to select 1,500 veterans and organize them into a reserve army, and have agreed to prepare 100,000 sacks within three days. After 8 p.m. on the 23rd, armed plainclothes soldiers were dispatched to guard all intersections between China and Japan. At all intersections within the Japanese concession, armed soldiers were dispatched to patrol with rifles and bayonets. The Japanese police station has decided to install iron fences at all intersections to prevent emergencies. Due to widespread rumors, the British and French concessions are also secretly on alert. It is rumored that Nakamura, the commander of the Japanese army stationed in Tianjin, will be ordered to go to Yuguan to command the attack on Jehol. (23rd, special dispatch)

(Beiping) The situation here is tense, like a powder keg. An incident seen from a Reuters window this morning is indicative of this. This morning, some infantry from the Japanese embassy guard were conducting a mock attack in front of Chinese civilians outside the boundary of 交民巷. The Chinese people now openly regard the Japanese as enemies, and their inner anger is evident. Fortunately, a squadron of Chinese cavalry patrolling the streets passed by and remained calm. If they had been slightly less patient, it would have inevitably caused trouble. The situation in Tianjin is similar. It is reported that Nakamura, the commander-in-chief of the Japanese army, has mobilized 1,500 reservists, which makes the number of Japanese soldiers stationed in Tianjin twice what it was before. (23rd, Reuters dispatch)

(Beiping) The enemy forces currently have more than 900 soldiers in Tanggu, 1,500 in Tianjin, and 500 in the expatriate volunteer army. There are 24 tanks and 5 armored vehicles in Tianjin. (23rd, special dispatch)

All news is disseminated by their own propaganda. Therefore, there have been rumors yesterday and today that Nanling and Beipiao have been occupied. Constitutional Drafting Committee 26

Discusses the Scope of Research for Constitution-Making

Decides to Divide into Four Groups to Study Specialized Issues

(Nanjing) The Legislative Yuan's Constitutional Drafting Committee held its third meeting at 3 p.m. on the 23rd. The attendees included Chairman Sun Ke, Vice Chairmen Zhang Zhiben and Wu Jingxiong, and committee members Xu Yuangao and 26 others. Wu Jingxiong chaired the meeting. Matters discussed: (1) It was decided to divide into four groups for research, with nine people in each group, to be responsible for researching several specialized issues. The list of each group will be designated by the President of the Legislative Yuan. (2) Next week's scope of research will include issues such as the form of government, sovereignty, territory, and flag colors. Those responsible for research are Zhang Zhiben, Wu Jingxiong, Jiao Yitang, Wu Shangying, Ma Yinchu, Fu Bingchang, Chen Zhaoying, and Xu Yuangao. (23rd, Central News Agency dispatch)

(Nanjing) When the Constitutional Drafting Committee met on the 23rd, it discussed the scope of research for constitution-making. The scope was tentatively set as (1) the form of government, sovereignty, territory, and flag colors; (2) the rights of the people; (3) the obligations of the people; (4) the National Assembly; (5) the division of powers between the central and local governments; (6) the central government system; (7) the provincial system; (8) the county system; (9) the power of constitutional interpretation and sanctions. It is reported that the President proposed the issue of national livelihood, and Xu Yuangao proposed adding the issue of the military system and the accounting system. How to allocate them needs to be decided at the next meeting. (23rd, Central News Agency dispatch)

The Ministries of Foreign Affairs and Industry Study

The Trade Plan with Russia

(Nanjing) Regarding the trade plan with Russia, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of Industry are conducting research. This method can correct the failures of past trade. This opinion has been submitted to the Executive Yuan and still needs to be decided by the Central Political Conference. (23rd, special dispatch)

(Nanjing) Our country's tea has always been sold to Russia. Even during the period of the severance of diplomatic relations between China and Russia, the amount imported into Russia was still considerable. The International Trade Bureau of the Ministry of Industry investigated that the value of tea imported into Russia last year was more than 60 million, and the supply still could not meet the demand. Russian merchants had no choice but to seek it from the Caucasus and Japan, but the quality of tea from the Caucasus and Japan was poor. According to an official from the Ministry of Industry, after the resumption of diplomatic relations between China and Russia, our country's tea exports to Russia will definitely be prosperous. This year, the minimum amount can be increased from 60 million to more than 70 million. (21st, special dispatch)

The Lawyers Association on the Gu Case

Requests a Change of Jurisdiction

Is Currently Collecting All Materials

Preparing to Draft an Indictment

(Nanjing) Regarding the case of Gu Zhutong illegally shooting Liu Yusheng, the National Lawyers Association, in order to safeguard the law and protect human rights, has filed a complaint with the judicial authorities, requesting that Gu Zhutong, who abused his power and illegally killed people, be prosecuted according to law. Liu Yangmin, a standing committee member of the association, said that they are currently collecting all materials and preparing to draft an indictment. The preliminary issue in this case is to request a change of jurisdiction, because according to the location of the defendant and the place where the crime was committed, the complaint should be filed with the Zhenjiang District Court. However, Gu is the highest administrative officer of Jiangsu Province, and there is a fear that he may use his power to interfere with the judiciary. Therefore, according to law, a change of jurisdiction is requested. After the association applies, the Zhenjiang District Court will submit a report to the Chief Prosecutor of the High Court, who will forward it to the Ministry of Judicial Administration for approval, and then ask the Supreme Court to designate it. After the association waits for the designated jurisdiction, it will file a complaint with the court, requesting the prosecutor to accept it and file a public prosecution according to law, to seek redress for Liu Yusheng. (23rd, special dispatch)

(Qingdao) The Jinpu Railway's eight newly purchased locomotives and eight open cars arrived in Qingdao on the 23rd via the Banertailailer. The railway dispatched 160 workers from the Jinpu Ji'nan maintenance factories to Qingdao to assist in the unloading. (Special dispatch on the 23rd)

Two Money Exchanges in Qingdao Fail 43

(Qingdao) The Yiju Zhan and Yiju Cheng money exchanges in the city secretly transported gold bars to Manchuria from Shanghai but were confiscated by the customs. Both exchanges closed today, losing over 200,000 yuan. (Special dispatch on the 23rd)

(Jinan) The Yijusheng Silver Shop in the city is bankrupt with a deficit of 300,000 yuan, causing losses to various silver and money exchange shops. Its affiliated company, Yiju Zhan, and Qingdao's Yijucheng have also collapsed. Currently, the silver and money exchange industry is not under customs control. The only peanut production in the province has suffered due to foreign merchants not buying, resulting in large stockpiles and price drops. Cotton yarn and cotton cloth prices have also dropped significantly due to the dumping of Japanese goods, causing major losses for those involved in these industries. (Special dispatch on the 23rd)

Bandits Discovered on Eastern Section of Longhai Railway 44

(Xuzhou) According to railway reports, bandits have been discovered near Zhuanzhuang on the eastern section of the Longhai Railway. Zhang Huatang's 44th Brigade has dispatched troops to suppress them, and the bandits have dispersed. (Special dispatch on the 23rd)

Large Batch of Rice Seeds Transported to Southern Henan for Distribution 45

(Xuzhou) Chairman Jiang, considering that although banditry in southern Henan has been suppressed, the disaster situation is severe, especially with farmers lacking seeds and fields lying fallow, making future disaster relief even more difficult, has allocated funds to purchase 1,000 piculs of rice seeds from Jiangnan. They will be transported to Xinyang and distributed to administrative commissioners for distribution in disaster areas. This large batch of rice seeds passed through Xuzhou on the 22nd from Nanjing to the west. The Ministry of Railways has ordered the Jinpu, Longhai, and Pinghan railways to transport them free of charge. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 23rd)

Signs of Disaster Again in Shaanxi Province This Year 46

(Xuzhou) Over a hundred refugees who escaped from Shaanxi Province arrived in Xuzhou on the evening of the 22nd. According to them, Shaanxi Province suffered a severe drought last year, with no harvest in Guanzhong. Although wheat was sown in the winter, the severe cold and lack of rain in March caused the wheat seedlings to wither and die, with most of them dying. Signs of disaster are appearing again this year. Currently, grain costs 28 yuan per picul, making life difficult, so many are fleeing. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 23rd)

Jiang's Address to Personnel in Two Departments 47

(Nanchang) Chairman Jiang summoned all staff members of the Post-Disaster Relief Association and the Party Affairs and Political Affairs Departments on the 22nd for an address, saying that the three forces of the Party, government, and military are the essential elements of revolution, and success cannot be achieved without any one of them. Past revolutions, especially bandit suppression, failed because the Party, government, and military could not advance simultaneously. He hoped that all comrades would work harder and more energetically, firstly, with the determination to work diligently and risk their lives; secondly, to maximize work efficiency; thirdly, to be realistic; and fourthly, to educate and organize the people. Chairman Xiong then delivered a reply on behalf of everyone. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 23rd)

Inauguration of the President of the Jiangxi High Court 48

Xiong Shihui Presides Over Oath and Delivers Admonition 49

(Nanjing) The President of the High Court, Lu Shizeng, held an inauguration ceremony on the 21st, presided over by Chairman Xiong, who delivered an admonitory speech, roughly stating that the past judicial circles in Jiangxi could be summarized by the four characters "wealth, nobility, longevity, and examination". (1) Money could win lawsuits, hence "wealth"; (2) Officials were mostly recommended by influential figures, hence "nobility"; (3) Security deposits could not be withdrawn for ten or twenty years, and lawsuits dragged on for seven deaths and eight lives, hence "longevity and examination". To correct these ills, one must use the methods of practical work, hard work, and quick work: using practical work to cure "wealth", using hard work to cure "nobility", and using quick work to cure "longevity and examination". (Central News Agency dispatch on the 23rd)

Hubei New Provincial Committee Scheduled to be Sworn In 50

(Hankou) Xia Douyin, Jia Shiyi, Li Shucheng, Li Fanyi, and various provincial committee members decided on the 23rd to officially establish the provincial government on the 1st and hold a swearing-in ceremony. They have telegraphed the Central Government to send a senior official to Hubei to preside over the oath. Cheng Tianfang is scheduled to arrive in Hankou on the 26th and could arrive on the 28th or 29th. (Special dispatch on the 23rd)

(Hankou) Xia Douyin hosted a banquet for Jia Shiyi, Li Fanyi, Li Shucheng, and others on the evening of the 23rd for preliminary discussions on the administrative guidelines of the new provincial government. (Special dispatch on the 23rd)

Shantou Investigates Dispute Over Seized Smuggled Sugar 51

(Shantou) The Municipal Party Department submitted a report to the East District Pacification Headquarters stating that inspectors, Guo and others, from the National Salvation Association reported that while inspecting in front of the Qilu Dadong Ice Factory, they seized Li Shiyi for smuggling smuggled sugar ashore from Fengshan Maru. Armed impostors threatened the inspectors with guns. Eight large packages of smuggled sugar were moved away, and only eight small packages were seized. Zhang Yuzheng brought the group, claiming to be a sea product donation inspector, and that the impostor, Liang, was responsible for the incident, undermining the national salvation movement. (Special dispatch on the 23rd)

Hangzhou Land Tax Postponed for One Month 52

Orders

The National Government issued an order on the 23rd, amending and promulgating the Examination Law, the Examination Supervision Law, and the Organization Law of the Classical Examination Committee. Another order was issued, abolishing the Special Examination Law and the Regional Examination Law.

Stalemate at the Disarmament Conference: Franco-German Discord Intensifies 53

Reuters dispatch from Geneva on the 23rd: It was learned today that a serious incident may occur at the Disarmament Conference because the German representative objected to the French proposal, stating that it was aimed at the German National Defense Force. Furthermore, the German proposal to first decide on the abolition of offensive weapons and then decide on the principles of army standards was deemed unfeasible by the chairman of the Disarmament Conference, Henderson, causing further distress to the German representative. (Editor's note: Last Friday, during the opening of the Geneva Disarmament Conference, the French representative and the German representative engaged in heated debate over the issue of Germany's "secret army", each refusing to yield. The French representative, Gude, stated that certain countries have certain groups that, although legal, can promote military spirit. The German representative, Nadolni, did not approve of the standardization of the army in his reply, strongly refuting the accusations against Germany without showing any weakness. Subsequently, French Prime Minister Daladier and Foreign Minister Peng Gu held lengthy talks on the matter in Paris. The German representative, Nadolni, also went to Berlin to consult with the government. Now, Peng Gu and Nadolni have both returned to Geneva.)

National News Agency dispatch from Geneva on the 23rd: The German representative to the Disarmament Conference, Nadolni, had a dispute with Henderson because Henderson opposed the German proposal to first discuss the abolition of offensive weapons and then address the issue of unifying the army system. This matter was hotly debated by representatives from various countries until late at night. The German representative sent a letter to Henderson last night, expressing his willingness to accommodate everything as long as it did not involve matters of principle.

National News Agency dispatch from Geneva on the 23rd: After an hour of talks between the German representative and Henderson this afternoon, the dispute that occurred in the General Committee last night was peacefully resolved. Henderson issued a statement clarifying that he inadvertently failed to consider Ambassador Nadolni's second request to speak, so the German representative will be at the top of the list of speakers at today's General Committee meeting.

Non-Aggression Pact Reaches Impasse 54

Major Powers to Negotiate Solutions 55

Reuters dispatch from Geneva on the 23rd: The Political Committee of the Disarmament Conference, which is trying to find a solution for European countries to agree on a non-aggression pact, is now at an impasse. The reason is that Germany fears that the newly established political convention is not sufficient to compensate for the guarantees of Locarno. The major powers concerned will hold a meeting to seek a common position.

The Dispute Over Security and Equality Transforms Into 56

A Dispute Over Military Systems and Weapons 57

National News Agency dispatch from Geneva on the 22nd: In today's General Committee of the Disarmament Conference, German representative Nadolni delivered a speech commenting on the French plan to unify the European army system, which attracted great attention from the members. Nadolni stated that any system that seeks to guarantee the security of all countries must be based on reducing the armaments of strong countries and seeking a balance of armaments, and then devise various plans to make all forces defensive in nature. Therefore, Germany believes that special attention must be paid to the following points: Firstly, the distinction between defensive and offensive nature is not as important in military systems as in armaments. Therefore, the most important thing is to abolish offensive weapons such as mobile artillery, tanks, and bomber aircraft. Secondly, regarding the issue of personnel in the army, it is not about adopting any specific recruitment system, but about greatly reducing the number of soldiers. On this level, colonial troops must be incorporated into the national army. Germany is currently prepared to discuss the French plan, but only after the aforementioned issues have been satisfactorily resolved. Therefore, he specifically summarized Germany's views on disarmament and proposed a resolution, which, in addition to elaborating on the aforementioned issues, proposed that the General Committee should consider the principles of abolishing all offensive weapons and restricting combat materials before discussing the French proposal to unify the military system, and instruct the Military Strength Committee to formulate regulations for reducing the number of land forces and balancing military strength in accordance with the principles of the Hoover Plan, and submit a report to the General Committee within a specified period.

Furthermore, in today's Aviation Expert Committee, French Air Force Chief Gude summarized a plan to establish an international airline to take over existing commercial aviation routes and be supervised by the League of Nations, but few other members agreed. The Dutch representative, Lottgen, stated that it is only necessary to formulate appropriate regulations for commercial aviation, which will be as effective as the French plan in preventing commercial aircraft from being converted for military use.

Havas dispatch from New York on the 23rd: Newly elected President Roosevelt recently announced that Davis will remain as the chief representative of the United States at the Geneva Disarmament Conference, but also stated that he wants to distinguish the issue of disarmament from the issue of economics. He believes that the reduction of world armaments is extremely important and hopes that the Geneva Disarmament Conference can achieve satisfactory results in a short period.

Roosevelt Gains Popular Support, New Government Cabinet List Drafted 58

Includes One Socialist Female Cabinet Member 59

General Approval for Hull and Woodin to Enter the Cabinet 60

Reuters dispatch from Washington on the 22nd: Elected President Roosevelt's appointment of Hull as Secretary of State and Woodin as Secretary of the Treasury has been celebrated by key figures in the Democratic Party, and even independent Republicans have praised it. This is enough to show that Roosevelt can win the hearts of the people. The House of Representatives has followed the Senate in voting to grant Roosevelt the power to reorganize the government and act expediently in order to fulfill his promise to reduce national spending by 25%. The House of Representatives has approved an amendment to the Treasury and Postal Service Appropriation Act, allowing the President to arbitrarily change various bureaus, which can only be stopped if two-thirds of both houses of Congress object. It is expected that Hoover will also agree to this.

National News Agency dispatch from New York on the 22nd: Reliable sources report that elected US President Roosevelt has drafted a new cabinet list and will have one female cabinet member, namely Ms. Pangins, who has been in charge of investigating labor conditions and living standards, serving as Secretary of Labor. The prepared cabinet list is as follows: Secretary of State Hull, Secretary of the Treasury Woodin, Secretary of War the Governor of Utah, Dunn, Secretary of the Navy Senator Swanson, Attorney General (similar to the Minister of Justice) Senator Walsh, Postmaster General Faley, Secretary of the Interior Ickes (a famous Republican leader), Secretary of Agriculture Tomoyan, Secretary of Commerce Rupp, and Secretary of Labor the socialist Ms. Pangins. Note that there are two Republicans in the cabinet, as the progressive faction of that party supported Roosevelt in the election, so they are being rewarded.

United States Navy 61

Spends More Money Chewing Candy 62

Than Maintaining the Navy 63

National News Agency dispatch from Washington on the 22nd: The chairman of the House Naval Affairs Committee, Vincent, stated in the House today that the United States spends more money chewing candy than maintaining the Navy. It would be ridiculous if Congress allowed the United States Navy to be inferior to other countries. He demanded that the United States Navy must be expanded to meet the strength allowed by the treaty, and must be expanded immediately so that the national defense forces can quickly reach the position allowed by the treaty. To prevent the effectiveness of the Navy from being reduced again, he will propose a bill in the next Congress to allocate 63 million yuan annually specifically for shipbuilding expenses.

French Senate Passes Finance Bill 64

Havas dispatch from Paris on the 23rd: The Senate has passed the finance bill by a majority of 230 votes to 70 votes. Before passing the finance bill, it rejected a motion to reduce military spending by 170 votes to 133 votes. Therefore, the bill will be presented again in the House of Representatives. The government did not raise the question of confidence in the Senate.

Central Europe Will Be More Eventful From Now On 65

Although the Franco-Austrian Arms Case Has Been Resolved 66

The Position of the Austrian Government Is Greatly Shaken 67

German and Italian Influence in Austria Is Increasingly Consolidated 68

Reuters dispatch from Vienna on the 22nd: The arms case, from the point of view of direct action, can be considered to be over, but it is expected that the impact of this matter on Austria will be far-reaching. The Austrian government now feels that it has been insulted by the dispatches from Britain and France. According to astute observers, the Austrian government may not last another month. Its position has been weakened by the arms case, and it is now facing severe opposition to the contract signed between the Austrian Trust Company and foreign creditors on January 10th of this year, and the Lausanne Treaty. It seems that the most recent impact of the dispatches from Britain and France is to consolidate the influence of Germany and Italy in Austria. People here are now freely expressing their opinions, saying that the number of Austrian loans provided by the League of Nations that France has assumed will be replaced by Germany. Vienna newspapers also carry news that German Chancellor Hitler has agreed to lend money to Austria, but on the condition that elections are held immediately and a mixed government is formed by the Christian Social Party and the National Socialist Party. The widespread rumor that a large amount of armaments from Czechoslovakia was transported to Yugoslavia via Austria, and the official admission of this fact, has also aroused public opposition.

Lowering Tariffs 69

Britain and the United States Agree 70

Reuters dispatch from London on the 22nd: Anglo-American war debt negotiations are unlikely to have any real action before Roosevelt takes office on March 4th. At the same time, British Ambassador Lindsay is currently consulting with Roosevelt and the new Secretary of State Hull. Today, the British House of Commons asked British Prime Minister MacDonald whether there was a way for the British Prime Minister to go to the United States to negotiate war debts. MacDonald replied in very clear terms that talks will resume immediately. Before the talks have a result, there can be no arrangements regarding procedures, but the British government will devote itself to the future economic conference in order to reduce general tax rates.

The Movement to Raise Silver Prices in the United States Congress Revived 71

The Main Motivation Is to Increase China's Purchasing Power 72

National News Agency dispatch from Washington on the 22nd: The US House Coinage Committee decided yesterday to shelve all currency reform plans, but due to the activities of the faction advocating higher silver prices, it reconsidered today and submitted the Sowers Act, as amended by the subcommittee, to the House of Representatives. The act stipulates that the Treasury Department is authorized to purchase a total of US$250 million worth of silver, with the silver price between 40 and 60 cents per ounce. The committee has requested the House Rules Committee to put it on the agenda so that it can be voted on in this Congress. The purpose of this case is not to inflate currency but to raise silver prices, so the amount of silver purchased is limited. It is also heard that the main motivation for raising silver prices is to increase China's purchasing power for American goods, thereby promoting trade with China.

China's Representative Makes Another Statement to Japan Six 73

The Spirit of the Treaty of Portsmouth

The Japanese representative also stated, "[China's current center embodies] Sovietism, thus posing a major crisis for the Far East." They further stated, "The reason this movement hasn't progressed faster is due to Japan's existence. At the very least, Soviet Russia respects Japan. If Japan were to leave, the red tide would engulf the Yangtze River basin immediately." They also claimed, "In short, Japan's current position is a solitary struggle to save the Far East from peril. The fact that Soviet Russia remains outside the League of Nations further exacerbates Japan's difficulties." Furthermore, they stated, "We have now reached a critical juncture for the nation's survival. The restoration of peace and order in the Far East is naturally not the concern of outsiders. Japan's past history has been praised by all. Therefore, Japan's knowledge of Far Eastern affairs, its methods for handling them, and its understanding of the other parties involved should be deeply trusted without question." From the above, it seems one can deduce Japan's profound fear of the spread of Sovietism. However, this is far from the truth. The Japanese are raising these alarmist claims merely as a convenient argument. We can see this from Japan's decision to implement its plan to militarily occupy Manchuria while China was fully engaged in military and financial efforts to eradicate the Red bandits in the Yangtze River region.

Although Japan has obstructed China's determination to eliminate the communist rebellion, China has still achieved remarkable success. General Chiang Kai-shek, the Commander-in-Chief of Bandit Suppression in the provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, has submitted a detailed report to the National Government on the achievements in bandit suppression since April. The government, on one hand, employs military force, and on the other hand, uses political methods, advancing on both fronts simultaneously. Therefore, the former bandit areas have now been restored to their original state.

In fact, from another part of the Japanese representative's speech, one can see that they themselves are not entirely convinced of Soviet Russia's potential intentions. The Japanese representative stated, "Soviet Russia has a considerable understanding of the Manchurian problem." They also said, "However, what we should be grateful to Soviet Russia for is that we not only need not fear the outbreak of war but also have a great opportunity to establish a peaceful understanding with each other." Not only that, but the Japanese representative even raised the possibility of a Japanese-Russian alliance as a kind of threat, saying, "If we can establish a firm agreement with Soviet Russia, regardless of anything else, then what will the situation be like afterward?" Isn't this something to be greatly concerned about?

In conclusion, the Japanese representative's policy is essentially a policy of intimidation towards all nations. However, even though they have violated their sacred promises, they can still leave fully satisfied. Consider their statement, "The Japanese government's actions, when judged under the League of Nations Covenant, should enjoy flexibility. This is something we should all recognize in common sense."

However, the principles on which the League of Nations is based must have universal applicability if we hope it can effectively serve world peace. It must be understood that the League of Nations Covenant is essentially the constitution of the world. Therefore, its interpretation should also be consistent. No matter how complex the situation of a particular case, the framework of the Covenant must not be damaged. If we create valid exceptions, then the nature of the issue itself is already an exception, and the complexity or difficulty of any issue is merely a matter of degree. If the League of Nations' primary foundation cannot be relied upon as a pillar of world justice and peace, then the guarantee of peace that the nations of the world have acquired at great cost and nurtured with their blood and sweat for ten years is likely not truly reliable.

The Japanese representative's statement that "the whole world is constantly changing" may indeed have some truth to it. However, with respect to the sanctity of the principles of the League of Nations, we can only solemnly tell the Japanese representative that any change or correction should not arise from violating international peace charters but should arise from complete respect for these charters. The peace of the whole world is our most sacred aspiration. (The End)

Supervisor

Liu E'qing's Interpellation Case 74

Disciplinary Cases Versus Impeachment Cases

The Difference Between Ten and One Hundred

Why Are Many Impeached Officials Delaying Execution?

Four Doubts About the Facts of Laws and Regulations

Beijing News: The Control Yuan, based on a written interpellation submitted by Control Commissioner Liu E'qing regarding cases of officials at all levels being impeached for violating the law and dereliction of duty, with few disciplinary agencies executing the punishments, immediately forwarded the interpellation to the National Government for review and implementation. The original text of the submission is as follows:

"[Regarding forwarding an interpellation: According to a written submission from Control Commissioner Liu E'qing, since the establishment of this Yuan, we have impeached officials at all levels who have violated the law and derelicted their duties. However, the powers stipulated by the Yuan's laws are limited to impeachment. As for adopting strict punishments to thoroughly eliminate corruption and improve the efficiency of political renewal, thereby fulfilling the purpose of supervisory powers, this depends entirely on the disciplinary agencies. Since the successive establishment of the Central Disciplinary Committee for Civil Servants and the Disciplinary Committee for Political Officials, the commissioners of this Yuan have been earnestly speaking out, believing that it would not be difficult to achieve the aforementioned aspirations. However, according to the recent statistics of this Yuan, the ratio of disciplinary cases to impeachment cases has become a difference between ten and one hundred. Among these cases, there are more than twenty cases impeaching political officials, yet no clear disciplinary measures have been determined, leading to criticism from the public, who claim that the supervisory agencies are equivalent to being set up in vain. The commissioners are also constantly troubled day and night, feeling fearful of dereliction of duty. Article 12 of the Impeachment Law states that if a disciplinary agency delays or suppresses a transferred case, the Control Yuan may interpellate. The commissioner hereby requests an interpellation in accordance with this law. In the past, during the imperial era, the law for ministers was used to instruct lesser officials to be incorruptible. Today's political officials are equivalent to the grand ministers and frontier officials of the past. If political officials are unlawful, yet ordinary civil servants are held responsible for being incorruptible, this is unfair according to legal principles. If the law is not enforced on powerful individuals, it is a sign of historical decline and disorder. If punishments are not strict on those close to power, it is a sign of collapsing discipline. If no impeached political official fails to avoid disciplinary measures, then the commissioners are merely holding the bamboo slips of history and accompanying the meals at the steps of the palace. How could they be compared to Zhang Gang's chariot, buried together in the capital? What can be said about the constant rule of national law? This is the first thing that greatly confuses the commissioner. The establishment of the Disciplinary Committee for Political Officials has been several months, yet the cases submitted by this Yuan are reportedly still under investigation or in the process of notifying the impeached individuals to submit their appeals. The cases impeached by this Yuan are inherently different in nature from those prosecuted by the courts. These procedures are already feared to be obstructive and inappropriate. Even if investigation and defense are deemed indispensable, the impeached cases have already been delayed for a long time. People have changed, and evidence has disappeared, like chariot tracks that have already passed, asking those on the road. The mud and snow have already been buried, investigating at the inns. How can it not be different? As for the impeached individuals, they may have stumbled due to other reasons, or they may have been promoted through connections, drifting like Hong Qiao, changing their names like Zhang Lu, or embellishing massacres as meritorious service in suppressing bandits, boasting of extortion as effective fundraising, manipulating documents while also bending the law, dreaming of corpses while also obtaining official positions. These situations are truly impossible to investigate and impossible to defend. The cases impeached by this Yuan are thus delayed repeatedly, and their effectiveness is completely lost. This is the second thing that greatly confuses the commissioner. Political officials bear the responsibility of being linked to the political situation. Appointments and dismissals have an impact on the current situation. This may be a general reason for delaying disciplinary measures. Furthermore, the current situation in various places is still precarious, and the joint rule of military and civilians has long become an intertwined situation. The central government is cautious in its actions, naturally having other reasons of its own. However, the commissioners, after comprehensively reviewing this internal situation, feel that it is unreasonable. Political officials, especially those related to the current political situation, should first rectify themselves and their subordinates. If they are ignorant of this principle and dare to violate the law and derelict their duties, then the central government enforcing the law to hold them accountable is a fundamental principle of establishing governance and employing people. Why should there be any considerations? In the past, during the era of warlords, local leaders held military power and had the constitution in their mouths. However, once a clear order was issued to condemn them, they still did not dare to not leave their posts in a simple carriage, submitting themselves for punishment. If today, there is still concern about disregarding the law and resisting orders, would this not undermine authority? Furthermore, the most severe punishment under the Disciplinary Law is merely dismissal from office. There is no execution in the marketplace, and there is no humiliation of being brought to court. What fears or hesitations prevent a clear disciplinary measure from being issued? This is the third thing that greatly confuses the commissioner. Since the national crisis, the National Government has relocated, and governance has lost its normal course. Corrupt officials have taken advantage of the situation, to the extent that it is shocking to hear. It is thought that the central government, with the national crisis at hand, aware of the duties of sparrows building nests and concerned about the plight of fish in the depths and birds in the thickets, is striving for broad tolerance, hoping to achieve a comprehensive effect. However, this intention is too circuitous and not aligned with the law. The failure of a nation is inherently due to corrupt officials. If all officials do not correct themselves, punishments are akin to tattooing. It is deeply believed that the national crisis arose from greedy and degenerate individuals. In the past, when the disaster of floods was imminent, it was calmed with four executions. When the crow did not fly at the national gate, it was shot down with one arrow. According to historical records, there were only instances of rectifying discipline to face the national crisis, and there were no instances of abandoning discipline due to the national crisis. This is the fourth thing that greatly confuses the commissioner. Regarding the four points above, whether they are the reasons for delaying and suppressing the cases of impeached political officials, the commissioner has repeatedly deliberated and is greatly puzzled. Knowing that disciplinary powers do not belong to this Yuan, how dare we presume to interfere? However, for the sake of national law and the responsibility of speech, having the power to interpellate according to law, we cannot remain silent. Therefore, we request that this be forwarded and instructed to be reviewed and replied to by the Disciplinary Committee for Political Officials." Based on this, it is appropriate to forward this to be reviewed and implemented in accordance with the law. Respectfully submitted to Lin, Chairman of the National Government.]"

On the 22nd, four bandit ships carrying over forty bandits arrived at the market town of Huangdai in the Suzhou countryside. Wuxi 76

Long-Distance Telephone Line Added Between Wuxi and Chengjiang

The local telegraph bureau has received an order from the Ministry of Communications to install a pair of long-distance telephone lines on the existing telegraph poles between Wuxi and Chengjiang to implement telephone communication. Nantong 78

Mutinying Soldiers of the 21st Division Disarmed

Fifty-three mutinying soldiers of the 21st Division, fleeing by sea, landed at Xiaomiao Hong in Qidong. Pinghu 79

Eighty-Three Teahouses in Total Boycott

The county previously established a temporary basic team, but there was no funding. The county authorities suggested that each teahouse collect one copper coin per pot of tea sold as a donation. The office ordered approval, and about a thousand gold coins were donated each month. Until the end of last year, the teahouse industry, suffering losses in business, requested the cessation of the levy, but this has not been approved. Later, the industry initiated the organization of a trade association and strongly argued with the authorities, but with insufficient reasons, there was no result. Starting on the 22nd, eighty-three teahouses in the urban area automatically stopped business, with signs posted at the doors saying, "District Chief reneged on agreement, business suspended" and "Stop business to live."

Xiaoshan 80

Fire in Waisha Village Kills Two

The home of Sha Min Zhang Jixian in Waisha Village in western Xiaoshan was set ablaze on the 21st midnight due to unattended fire in the kitchen. The fire then spread, burning down seven tile-roofed houses and ten thatched huts, burning to death a seven-year-old girl and a three-year-old boy. Three pigs and three sheep were also killed, and items worth more than five thousand gold were burned.
