Local News

City Federation Advocates Implementing Unified Resistance Against Japan 81

| Letter to President Song Dai and Appeal to Citizens |

The Shanghai Special District Citizens' Federation yesterday, for the sake of implementing unified resistance against Japan, sent a special telegram to Song Dai, President of the Executive Yuan, and issued an appeal to all citizens. The original texts are excerpted as follows:

Telegram to the Executive Yuan of the National Government in Nanjing, Hon. Song Dai, President of the Executive Yuan,

Ever since the Japanese army invaded and occupied the three northeastern provinces on September 18th of the year before last, due to the non-resistance of the border defense officials, the territories have been lost and have not yet been recovered. How painful is this to the people! However, in terms of diplomacy, through your efforts to coordinate beforehand and respond to emergencies, strategizing and assisting the diplomatic authorities in appealing to the League of Nations, after seventeen months of effort, the draft report of the League of Nations' Committee of Nineteen has been obtained and will soon be passed by the General Assembly. Although the suggestions may not be entirely to our liking, with this result, diplomacy cannot be said to be unsuccessful. Because the Japanese military action in the three northeastern provinces is not legitimate self-defense, our country's territorial sovereignty in the three northeastern provinces is recognized by all countries, and the people's boycott of Japanese goods is a retaliation against Japan's illegal force, this has become an ironclad case. The Japanese soldiers, with a rubber stamp in hand, do not reflect on their past mistakes and are again plotting to invade Jehol. Knowing that war is ultimately inevitable, you spared no effort in traveling long distances, flying to Beiping day and night, and rushing to Jehol to encourage military morale and plan for war expenses, representing the central government in announcing both internally and externally. The Japanese were thus enraged, and the world took notice. This is the time when our country is turning from adversity to prosperity, and the people have a reason to resist Japan. How uplifted are the citizens of Shanghai! However, since Japan is mobilizing the military and financial resources of the entire country to come, how can we not have wartime controls to defend ourselves? As the head of the Executive Yuan, how can you unite all departments into one, issuing orders that are carried out, avoiding mistakes in military opportunities, and protecting the country? This must already be clear in your mind, and there is no need for the people to worry. However, there are some things that I cannot help but say. The people's supply is naturally a duty that should be fulfilled, and rapid and free transportation is especially what the people earnestly pray for. Because in a war against Japan, the government and the people are one body, and it is not easy to clearly distinguish between them. If transportation is delayed even slightly, it will most easily delay military opportunities. This is one. Regarding foreign trade, our country has always been freely operated by the people. The latest modern policy has adopted state-owned enterprises, and various countries every time adopt intervention methods during wartime, precisely to prevent providing resources to the enemy and to limit the people's unnecessary consumption. Please find ways to implement this. This is two. In your speech to reporters on February 22nd, you said that people's organizations are too complex, which reduces the concentration of strength. This is truly insightful. However, on the one hand, mass organizations should strive for unified wartime organization, and on the other hand, the government must also be in close contact with such organizations, providing convenience and information, so that it can be like the body directing the arm and the arm directing the finger, without any hindrance. This is three. If we can unite and implement wartime controls, the Japanese army within our country will be insufficient to drive away. We respectfully submit this telegram, hoping that you will take it into consideration. The Shanghai Citizens' Federation respectfully bows.

Appeal to Citizens:

The Shanghai Citizens' Federation Appeals to All Citizens to Implement Unified Resistance Against Japan.

Since the draft report of the League of Nations' Committee of Nineteen was published, although it still needs to be passed by the General Assembly, Japan's invasion of our country, with the three northeastern provinces being our country's territory, has been recognized by the world. Therefore, recovering our territory is the sole responsibility of our people. However, our people, in this time of national survival crisis, have not yet completely eradicated the bad habits of being polite. They are strict with others and lenient with themselves, strict with the government and lenient with themselves. The government's resistance against Japan has already progressed from declarations, reports, talks, and telegrams to burying its head in practical work. President Song Dai's recent words and actions can be seen as evidence of this. Although the transportation authorities have not yet regarded supplies for resisting Japan as related to military opportunities and transported them as quickly as possible, they will soon be able to implement wartime controls for military needs. However, no matter how the people's movement to resist Japan progresses, the construction of aircraft is indeed an essential tool for resisting Japan's air defense. However, this cannot be achieved by simply naming planes or making pledges on paper. Even if there are funds, due to the limitations of time and space, it cannot be achieved overnight. Since Japan's military action against Jehol is already in full swing, the lesser of two evils and the more urgent of two matters should be chosen. Therefore, providing funds to support the anti-Japanese forces on the Jehol border is the most important thing to do today. However, there are many anti-Japanese fundraising organizations established in Shanghai, which not only disperses efforts and divides energy but also makes it impossible for donors to know where to contribute. The association believes that the citizens of Shanghai as the leaders of China, should immediately adopt wartime controls to strengthen their real strength and benefit military opportunities, avoiding delaying the country. Therefore, we present several matters for your information: (1) The citizens of Shanghai should immediately establish a wartime organization and be directed by this organization as a whole. (2) All anti-Japanese fundraising organizations should immediately merge into one and be governed by this wartime organization as a whole. (3) All donations should strive to correct the previous shortcomings of relying solely on overseas Chinese and small and medium-sized citizens. (4) All citizens should reduce clothing, food, housing, transportation, electricity, telephones, etc. Whatever can be saved should be saved. During the European War, the citizens of Shanghai should remember the circumstances of Westerners saving electricity. (5) We ask the government to quickly implement a policy of controlling foreign trade in order to facilitate distinguishing needs. (6) All who want to buy necessary goods should buy them from stores that have proof of having no Japanese goods, and they should especially buy domestic goods and buy them from domestic goods companies. (7) We hope that all citizens will actively engage in production and actively reduce non-productive behavior. It is best if labor disputes, rent disputes, and various economic relations can maintain the status quo. Otherwise, the interests of the majority should be sought. Fellow citizens of Shanghai, now is a time of crisis for survival! Only with a country can there be a home, and only with territory can there be benefits. If we continue to wait and see, compete for petty gains, and seek private interests, when the country is shattered, those who think they are prosperous will be the first to suffer. We hope that the leaders of the city will rise up and initiate this. This association will follow behind them, holding the reins to follow. We specially draft this letter to present this idea. We respectfully ask for your consideration.

all the stallholders in the Hongkou Triangle Market, about 2,000 households, immediately gathered to discuss donating money to purchase airplanes for national defense. On the spot, 21 stallholders signed up voluntarily to join the Aviation Association as special members, including Zhang Zongbao, Xue Yongxiang, Qian Wenqing, Xu Genquan, Pan Amao, Qian Xianglang, Ji Weixin, Tang Heshen, and Li Guoqing. Nine people volunteered to be ordinary members, including Qian Jinqing, Zhang Zhiliang, Gu Ayou, Gong Tinghua, Shen Shijie, Wang Ruiqi, Zhou Xianglang, Ji Sanlang, Zhu Jinbiao, Bao Hanshan, and Zou Qisheng. In addition to twelve people like Mrs. Zhang, it was also proposed that each stallholder contribute one cent of silver (equivalent to three copper coins) per day, and that one person be elected every Saturday to settle the accounts and remit them to the Aviation Association or the collection agency. On the same day, more than 200 households voluntarily pledged to donate. If all households can pledge to donate in the future, about 500 yuan can be obtained in donations every month.

Customs Adds Dedicated Wireless Radio Station 96

Seeking Speed and Efficiency in Transmitting Smuggling Information

In order to strictly prevent tax evasion, the National Government has approved the Customs to add a dedicated wireless radio station to seek speed and efficiency in transmitting smuggling information and dispatching coastal patrol boats. It is reported that the Customs authorities now plan to set up general stations in Yantai, Shanghai, Xiamen, and the Chinese boundary of Kowloon, and branch stations in Shantou, Haikou, and Qiongzhou. In the future, if there is a need to add more stations, it will be extended to other ports. The radio waves of each station have a limited range, as they are only used by the Customs to transmit messages between the various stations and patrol boats, which can be relayed to each other.

Naval Gunboats Launched Yesterday 97

Commander Chen Daopei Reports on the Process

Completion Expected at the End of May for Coastal Defense Patrol

The Navy Department's newly built Ning-class gunboats, except for the Jiangning and Hainan, which were launched on New Year's Day and incorporated into the Coastal Defense Patrol, had their sister gunboats, Funing and Suining, launched yesterday. The details are recorded as follows:

Launching of Two Ships

The Ning-class gunboats were originally planned to be ten ships, specializing in the Coastal Defense Patrol, for coastal anti-piracy. Apart from the Jiangning and Haining, which have been launched and put into use, the Funing and Suining are 130 feet long, 20 feet wide, 300 tons in tonnage, 7 feet in draft, and have a speed of 12 nautical miles per hour. They are armed with two 3-inch guns and three machine guns. The new construction began in October of the 21st year. After launching, they will be docked on the riverbank of the shipyard to install machinery. Completion is scheduled for the end of May. The remaining six Ning-class gunboats will continue to be built so that they can be used as soon as possible.

Ceremony Very Simple 98

The sister gunboats Funing and Suining held a launching ceremony at 11:30 AM yesterday at the Jiangnan Shipyard in Gaochangmiao. Due to the national crisis, all ceremonies were simplified. Commander Chen Daopei, Chief of the Patrol Wu Zhennan, Chief of the New Ship Construction Office Zeng Guocheng, and more than 50 others were present. Commander Chen Daopei chaired the ceremony and reported on the progress of the new construction. Then, aides Zheng Xianghan and Chen Daxian of the Training Fleet threw bottles. The ceremony concluded at 12:00 noon.

Inspecting Concession Factories 99

After the Zhengtai Rubber Factory Tragedy

The Municipal Government Believes Active Action is Necessary

A Central News Agency report stated: "Regarding the inspection of factories in this city, the urban areas have already been completed. However, the concession areas have not been implemented due to the obstruction of the two concession authorities. After the unprecedented tragedy of the cylinder explosion at the Zhengtai Rubber Factory No. 1 on Tangshan Road, which burned to death more than one hundred male and female workers, the municipal government of this city, in addition to expressing condolences, also believes that it is necessary to protect the safety of workers in factories in the concession areas, and that an immediate inspection is necessary. It plans to continue to negotiate actively with the concession authorities based on the regulations of the Factory Law, so as to complete the inspection of factories in this city in the shortest possible time and seek safety for all workers in the city."

Li Ting'an Discusses the Importance of Factory Hygiene 102

In response to the Zhengtai Factory Incident

Following the fire at the Zhengtai Rubber Factory on Tangshan Road, which resulted in the deaths of over one hundred workers and the loss of more than two hundred thousand yuan in capital, Director of the Bureau of Health, Mr. Li Ting'an, issued the following statement: "While the modern era is one of machine production, the application of machines still relies on workers. Therefore, workers are of utmost importance in production, and promoting industry must prioritize labor hygiene. Our country's factory laws already contain provisions regarding worker safety, hygiene, and limitations on the work hours of child and female laborers. However, it is regrettable that very few factories in our country currently comply with these regulations. The recent tragedy at the Zhengtai Rubber Factory has prompted the following reflections: (1) If the factory had implemented labor hygiene measures, this tragedy would not have occurred. The meaning of labor hygiene extends far beyond merely treating workers' illnesses. All factors that could harm workers' health and lives should be prevented, and specialized personnel should be employed to conduct regular inspections to reduce the risk of fire, floods, injuries, infectious diseases, and other hazards. (2) Our country's industry is in urgent need of promotion. Therefore, effective measures should be taken to ensure factory hygiene, so that factories can profit and workers' lives can be secured. The Zhengtai Rubber Factory tragedy, in which both the factory and the workers suffered enormous losses, should serve as a profound lesson for all those in our country who aspire to contribute to industry. However, the Zhengtai Factory is merely unfortunate to be the first to suffer such a disaster. In all fairness, the number of factories with similar latent dangers is far too numerous to mention. Therefore, it would be inappropriate to single out the Zhengtai Factory for criticism." Director Li also stated that labor hygiene should be jointly administered and implemented by factories and workers under the guidance of administrative agencies such as the Bureaus of Health and Social Affairs. This would likely be effective. He plans to exchange views with the Director of the Bureau of Social Affairs and convene a meeting of the city's industrial sector at an opportune time to find ways to establish such a system. The benefits of labor hygiene can be divided into three aspects: For the factory, it eliminates unexpected losses of assets (such as the reported financial loss of over two hundred thousand yuan at the Zhengtai Factory) and reduces losses in work efficiency (as the replacement of injured or sick workers by others can result in a decrease in proficiency and efficiency). For society, it reduces the losses from disability and death and preserves some of the productive capacity of society. For workers, it prevents unexpected disasters and illnesses, preserving their ability to save money. Therefore, labor hygiene is a crucial task that our country must address immediately. It is hoped that this message will be conveyed to the industrial and labor sectors, who will work together to this end. This Bureau is deeply committed to providing sincere guidance.

Rice Merchants in Northern Shanghai Aid the Petition for Level Measures and Funnels 106

Document Presented to the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs

The Shanghai Northern Rice Transporters United Association submitted a document to the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs yesterday, stating: "Submitting this document to request a swift resolution to the issue of rice measures, to end the disputes and avoid affecting the people's food supply. Since the fifteenth year of the Republic [i.e., 1926], disputes over rice measures have occurred continuously. This is a phenomenon unique to this area. The root cause lies not in the system of measuring instruments, but in whether the measurers are using 'tricks.' In the past, there were occasional unscrupulous market elements who used 'heavy in, light out' tricks to deceive customers, but once their schemes were exposed, their reputation would be ruined. Therefore, honest merchants were ashamed to engage in such practices. However, since the poor harvest and high rice prices in the fifteenth year of the Republic, this kind of fraudulent practice has emerged, and disputes have suddenly arisen, forming a widespread and shameful custom. They are shamelessly abandoning commercial ethics and sinking into depravity. The association has repeatedly protested in the past and has always been treated fairly by your bureau. However, although there has been temporary peace, the old problems soon reappear, leading to resistance from southern Shanghai, and the disturbances have spread and have not been resolved. If fundamental treatment is not applied, the people's livelihood will suffer greatly. The association has previously submitted suggestions to strictly prohibit measurers from using 'tricks' and to support the independent profession of measurers. Now, just as the new system of measures is beginning to be implemented, the disturbances over rice measures have also arisen. This proves that it is not a matter of the measuring instrument system, but whether the measurers are using 'tricks.' The rice merchants in southern Shanghai advocate the use of level measures and funnels, which is the fairest way to eliminate the malpractice of 'heavy' and 'light' measures. The association deeply sympathizes with this proposal. As for rice firms and dealers, they are intermediaries between rice transporters and rice shops. The most appropriate method is to have all parties present at the time of measurement to supervise each other. As for the rice shops, it is insufficient for them to measure the rice on their own when the rice carts arrive. This responsibility is inefficiently handled by both the measurers and the transporters. Originally, this was only to prevent malpractices from occurring en route by the delivery person. Therefore, the action of rice shops measuring rice is absolutely unrelated to the transporters and measurers. Recently, rice merchants in southern Shanghai have been forced to stop loading rice, and rice merchants in northern Shanghai also share their concerns. However, to protect the food supply of the city's residents, the association is actively encouraging rice merchants to wait patiently for a resolution. If the situation is prolonged, the disturbances will inevitably spread, and the resolution will become more difficult. Therefore, we specially request your bureau to provide a fundamental resolution as soon as possible, so as to achieve permanent peace and benefit the future of the rice industry and the food supply of the people. We eagerly await your response. Sincerely, the Shanghai Northern Rice Transporters United Association to Director Wu of the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs."

The Ministry of Industry Explains the Procedures for Branch Offices of Commercial Firms to Join Associations 107

Branch offices can join trade associations.

If there is no association, they can become merchant members of the chamber of commerce.

The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs received Order No. 4459 from the Municipal Government yesterday, stating: "Approved the Ministry of Industry's Commercial Document No. 16088, regarding the reply to the matter of inquiry from the National United Association of Match Manufacturers regarding whether branch offices or agencies can join industrial and commercial trade associations. Requested investigation and reply, etc. Approved. Upon investigation, if the branch offices or agencies mentioned in the original document are branch offices of companies or firms, they can be regarded as companies or firms and join trade associations. However, if there are fewer than seven businesses in the same industry within a region, an association cannot be legally formed, so participation is out of the question. For the local chamber of commerce, they can still join as merchant members. Approved the above. Correspondingly reply, requesting investigation and instructions for compliance, etc. Approved. Upon investigation, this case was previously forwarded to the government by your bureau and was duly consulted and instructed. Now, the above is approved. Correspondingly order your bureau to comply immediately and instruct for notification. This order."

The Committee Refusing Water Cutoffs Held Its First Meeting Yesterday 110

Petitioning the Municipal Government and Other Places Today

Informing Tenants to Vow to Fight to the End

The Real Estate Association Asks Feng Bingnan to Mediate

Ever since the British Shanghai Waterworks Company, accompanied by armed Chinese and Western detectives, cut off the main water pipes in Shuncheng Lane and other places on Yangshupu Road in the Eastern District and filled them with asphalt and gravel, it has aroused the resentment of the residents. Representatives were dispatched to the Shanghai Municipal Council and the water company to petition, but the Shanghai Municipal Council made no concrete response. According to the water company, the installation of water meters was in accordance with the instructions of the Shanghai Municipal Council, and the company's finances are quite strained due to the cost of installing water meters, which is over one hundred thousand taels of silver. Therefore, it is difficult to reduce water rates, and no result was achieved. At 8:45 p.m. the day before yesterday, two detectives even stopped people from drawing water by the Taiping tap and locked the tap. The water users were detained in the police station and were only released on bail after a large number of tenants demanded their release. The tenants of the lane, fearing that they would not be able to cook their meals if this continued, convened an autonomous tenant meeting yesterday and decided to contact the twenty-nine water cutoff lanes in the eastern district of Shanghai to carry out large-scale and active actions. They also decided to form the Shanghai Eastern Shuncheng Lane Committee Refusing Water Cutoffs and will submit documents to the Municipal Government, the Bureau of Social Affairs, the Municipal Party Headquarters, the Council of Councilors, the Taxpayers Association, the Tenant Union, and the Citizens Union today to request intervention and assistance. Notices will also be posted in the lane. The details of each item are recorded below.

Committee Meeting 111

The Shanghai Eastern Shuncheng Lane Committee Refusing Water Cutoffs held its first meeting at 8 p.m. yesterday at the Tenant Self-Government Association in the lane, chaired by Ding Qun. The following was discussed: (1) Name: It was decided to name it the Shanghai Eastern Shuncheng Lane Committee Refusing Water Cutoffs. (2) Organization: It was decided to establish a standing committee, divided into one office and four departments: 1. Secretariat, 2. General Affairs Department, 3. Propaganda Department, 4. Public Relations Department, 5. Disciplinary Department. (3) Standing Committee Members: It was decided that each committee member would nominate five people: Ding Fangqun, Gong Leitong, Wang Yiting, Zhou Binzhang, Qu Huaqing, etc. (4) Number of People in Each Department and Selection of Personnel: It was decided: 1. General Affairs Department: three people: Wang Yiting, Zhang Lianchuan, Hou Jiahai; 2. Secretariat: two people: Gong Leitong, Gao Yiqun; 3. Propaganda Department: four people: Ding Fangqun, Xu Zhaonan, Gong Yuting, Chen Nanshan; 4. Public Relations Department: five people: Zhou Zhang, Sun Hengzhan, Wang Shicheng, Zhang Quanda, Sun Yanhui; 5. Disciplinary Department: five people: Qu Huaqing, He Yuanliang, Zhang Yongmin, Cui Wanru, Yao Tingyu. (5) Contacting Various Groups to Proceed Unanimously: It was decided that the Public Relations Department would handle this in conjunction with the Propaganda Department. (6) Filing with Various Agencies and Petitioning: It was decided that the Secretariat and Public Relations Department would handle this. (7) Maintaining Security: It was decided that the Disciplinary Department would handle this. (8) Committee Expenses: It was decided that each committee member would temporarily advance five jiao. (9) Standing Committee Dates: It was decided that meetings would be held every Wednesday and Saturday. (10) Committee Dates: It was decided that meetings would be held every Saturday. (11) Announcing Notices and Slogans.

Notifying Tenants 112

The Shanghai Eastern Shuncheng Lane Committee Refusing Water Cutoffs hereby notifies: Esteemed elders, brothers, sisters, and fellow citizens, I respectfully inform you that since the Shanghai January 28th Incident, all industries have declined, workers have lost their jobs, wages have decreased, and the people have suffered greatly. The British Shanghai Waterworks Company, however, at this time, followed the instructions of the Shanghai Municipal Council to install water meters and greatly increase water prices, increasing the amount previously paid by tenfold. The people are suffering and cannot afford this. In the midst of ongoing negotiations, the Shanghai Municipal Council suddenly sent armed detectives to accompany the Shanghai Waterworks Company to cut off the water. Water and fire are essential for the people's daily life, and cutting off the water with force is tantamount to killing the people. Therefore, the people of our lane are united and have formed the Committee Refusing Water Cutoffs. In addition to requesting assistance from various agencies, we are also uniting with the people of Shanghai to jointly resist the Shanghai Waterworks Company's price increase and oppose the Shanghai Municipal Council's armed water cutoffs. We also hope that our elders, brothers, sisters, and fellow citizens will not cause disputes due to competing for water, but will remain calm and wait for a resolution. This committee vows to fight to the end. This is specially notified.

Some Slogans 113

The committee decided on the following slogans:

(1) Residents of eastern Shanghai, unite and organize a Committee Refusing Water Cutoffs! (2) Oppose water cutoffs, demand immediate water supply! (3) Oppose increasing water prices! (4) Oppose the waterworks company that disregards the lives of the people! (5) Oppose the Shanghai Municipal Council's armed water cutoffs! (6) The people spontaneously organize water protection teams! (7) Citizens of Shanghai, unite and organize a Committee Refusing Water Cutoffs! etc. Starting today, these will be posted in various lanes to urge residents to unite and fight to achieve the ultimate goal.

Requesting Intervention 114

The Sixth District Branch of the Citizens' Association received a letter yesterday from tenants' representatives Sheng Xinru, Qiu Jialiang, Chen Baoxing, Zhang Hechun, Chen Xintian, etc. of Jingqing Lane, stating that their lane was forcibly cut off by the waterworks company on the morning of the 20th, causing panic among the residents and creating dangerous situations. Therefore, the representatives, Qiu Jialiang, etc., were elected, and although they negotiated with the Shanghai Municipal Council to temporarily open the Taiping tap along the main road at the entrance of the lane, it was insufficient for the large number of residents, leading to disputes and injuries. If the original situation is not restored as soon as possible, there will be no water to drink, which is a matter of life. The association will send the above information to the Chinese Taxpayers Association and the Citizens' General Union to request serious negotiations with the Shanghai Municipal Council to protect the lives of the people and ensure social stability.

Feng's Mediation 115

According to news from the Real Estate Association, Kui Yanfang, Bao Luoyan, Li Pahan, etc. invited Feng Bingnan yesterday to negotiate with the Shanghai Municipal Council water company, etc., in the hope of resolving the situation as soon as possible and avoiding the residents' panic over the water cutoff. Feng stated that the matter concerned the safety of the citizens and he would do his utmost to argue with all relevant parties based on reason and promised to respond to the association next Wednesday.

Another Dispute 116

According to the Guowen News Agency, a Cantonese woman in Jingqing Lane on East Seward Road was blocked by a Shanghai Municipal Council worker yesterday while using the Taiping tap on the street as usual due to the water cutoff by the waterworks company. Due to the language barrier, a conflict ensued. The owner of the Yuanchang Porcelain Shop came out to mediate, but the worker turned his anger on the owner of the Yuanchang Shop. A patrolman arrived and wanted to take the owner of the Yuanchang Shop to the police station, but the owner refused, and his clothes were torn in the dispute. They eventually went to the police station but were soon released. The worker also bled from his teeth due to the conflict.

Jiangsu High Court to Hear Cases Yesterday 123

Gold Mountain Child Murder Case 124

Xia Aqing Denies Previous Confession

Suzhou Dispatch: The case of Wang Diqing from Gold Mountain being killed by Wang Tao, Xia Aqing, Zhang, and others has already been judged. Wang Yutian, the accountant, was arrested and sentenced to death by the Gold Mountain County for suspicion of conspiracy to murder. Wang refused to accept the verdict and appealed to the Jiangsu High Court. Two hearings were held in February and March of last year. However, due to the files of Wang Tao and others being at the Supreme Court and not yet transferred, the hearings were postponed. The Jiangsu High Court held a hearing yesterday afternoon, presided over by Judge Song Yuan and others. The defendant, Wang Yutian, appointed Gao Ruoxiang and Wang Zengxian (represented by Qu Yue, entrusted by lawyers) as lawyers to defend him in court. During the interrogation, Wang denied conspiring to kill Wang Diqing and detailed his return to Song, his travels to collect debts, and his recuperation from illness. Wang Tao denied having an affair with Wang Yutian. Xia Aqing also denied stating in the first trial that Wang Tao relayed Wang Yutian's urging to kill Wang Youqing. After thorough arguments by Wang and Gao, Judge Song announced the end of the debate and adjourned the court.

Labor Dispute at the Great China Overshoe Factory over Union Organization 125

| Conflict Between Workers and Manager |

The Great China Overshoe Factory, located on Xingjiazhai Road in Zhabei, employs approximately two hundred male and female workers. Recently, the factory was ordered by the city's Party Headquarters to reorganize the workers' union and place it under the jurisdiction of the Fourth District Rubber Workers' Union by the 26th of this month. Workers Zhang Linbing, Wu Fushou, and others were appointed as organizers to handle the re-registration and other matters. Yesterday afternoon, around 3 PM, Zhang and others went to each male and female worker to record their names and numbers for registration. However, one female foreman suspected that Zhang and others had ulterior motives and immediately reported to the factory manager, Yang Yongyi. Yang immediately summoned Zhang and others for a discussion, asking if they intended to incite a labor strike. Zhang and others immediately denied this, but Yang remained unconvinced, leading to a verbal conflict. Yang grabbed Wu Fushou and slapped him twice, tearing his clothes in the process of the dispute. Zhang and others argued that the union organization was ordered by the authorities and not a private undertaking, and that physical assault was unjustified. They then took Yang to the First Branch of the Fifth District Public Security Bureau for investigation. After questioning by Chief Liang, the bureau attempted mediation but failed, and the group of people was transferred to the General Bureau for further investigation.

Page 10

Homecoming of War Orphan Lu Junwu, Son of Battalion Commander Lu Bin Who Died in the Shanghai Battle 126

Returned to the Clan After Verification by Jiang, Cai, and Others

Lu Bin was from Yixing, Suzhou. During the Shanghai Battle, he served as the deputy battalion commander in the Sixth Regiment of the Seventy-eighth Division of the Nineteenth Route Army. On the night of January 28th, his battalion was stationed in the area of Tiantong'an Road and Baoxing Road when the battle broke out. Their defense line was the first to be attacked. The battalion commander bravely moved back and forth on the front lines, diligently directing the troops. Unfortunately, he was fatally struck by a stray bullet and died. His remains were transported back to his hometown for burial by his brother, Lu Jie. Later, upon his mother's orders, Lu Jie went to Guangdong to retrieve the widow, Shi Yuehao, and the orphaned son, Lu Junwu. However, upon arriving in Guangdong, Shi had already become involved with Yu Keming, an employee of a bureau in Guangzhou. Upon hearing of Lu Jie's arrival, she avoided meeting him. After much effort, Lu Jie finally found her, but Shi not only refused to return to Suzhou but also denied that Junwu was Lu Bin's orphaned son. Left with no choice, Lu Jie filed a lawsuit in the Guangzhou District Court and the High Court. Former Nineteenth Route Army Commander Jiang, Commander Cai, Division Commander Qu, Brigade Commander Zhang, and Chief Secretary of the Headquarters Zhu Jiasheng all sent letters to the court, proving that Junwu was indeed Lu Bin's orphaned son. After half a year of litigation, the case was finally closed. Lu Jie has now returned to Suzhou with the orphaned son, Junwu, and will soon return to his hometown to rejoin the clan.

Congestion of Wheat Ships on the Huangpu River 127

Slow Unloading Leads to Increased Accumulation

Insufficient Floating Docks on the Huangpu River

The Mainland News reports that there is a recent surge in the number of wheat ships on the Huangpu River, causing considerable congestion. There is a shortage of suitable floating docks for the wheat ships to berth. With more ships expected to arrive, the Huangpu River will soon be full. Currently, there are five wheat ships docked in Shanghai. Since the beginning of the year, thirty-seven ships have arrived, and six more are expected by the end of the month. Each ship can carry approximately seven thousand tons of wheat, mostly from Australia, with some from Canada and Argentina. The congestion of wheat imports is reportedly due to a domestic wheat harvest that is only one-third of the usual yield. However, some of the wheat is believed to be destined for the north to supply food to the Chinese troops in Rehe. The congestion of wheat ships on the Huangpu River is not only due to the large number of arrivals but also to the slow unloading process and the lack of storage space at flour mills. In Western countries, wheat is unloaded using machinery that sucks it into elevators and transports it to storage silos, relying entirely on mechanical power and completing the unloading in one or two days. In Shanghai, however, the wheat needs to be bagged, transported onto barges, and then transferred to the mills, which typically takes ten to eleven days to unload each ship, rarely completing the process in less than a week. Combined with the recent surge in wheat ship arrivals, this has further exacerbated the congestion on the Huangpu River.

University Student Dies by Poisoning 128

Luo Qiheng from Gaoxian, Sichuan

Suspected Suicide Due to Financial Difficulties

Luo Qiheng, a university student from Gaoxian, Sichuan, aged twenty-eight, lived alone in a small room in the Jinderi building, No. 7 Jinshenfu Road, French Concession, renting from Gu Kaiyuan from Nanjing for five yuan per month. He moved in last September and left the house every morning at 11 AM, returning between 11 PM and 12 AM. He ate at the Qiangpu Sichuan Restaurant at No. 16 Dapufang, Dapu Bridge, and was from the same hometown as the restaurant owner, Xiong Shengtin. For the past three days, the sub-landlord noticed that Luo had not been going out and that there was no movement or sound from his room, suspecting he was ill. On the morning of the 22nd, at 12 PM, he knocked on the door, but there was no response. He pried open the door and found Luo had died from poisoning, with blood foam coming from his mouth. It was unknown when he had died. The sub-landlord reported to the police, who sent detectives to investigate. Several letters were found in the room, including one from his brother criticizing his extravagance, his multiple marriages and divorces with women in Shanghai, and urging him to return home as soon as the remittance arrived. Besides the bed, bedding, and mosquito net, there were no other belongings. It was inferred that Luo committed suicide due to financial difficulties. The body was taken to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Mortuary for an autopsy. Since there were no relatives of the deceased in Shanghai, a report was filed with the Second Special District Court yesterday morning. Prosecutor Deng Baosun arrived at the mortuary to confirm that the death was indeed due to poisoning. According to the sub-landlord Gu Kaiyuan's account of the discovery, it was decided that the body would be photographed and then collected and buried by the Tongren Fuyuan Hall, pending identification by relatives.

Bidding for Yuehan Railway Project in Shanghai 129

The Yuehan Railway has been under construction since the late Qing Dynasty, lasting more than thirty years with repeated setbacks, never completed. By 1930, the sections completed include the northern section from Hankou to Changsha, totaling 385 kilometers, called the Xiang'e section; and the southern section, initially built by Guangdong Province from Guangzhou to Shaoguan for 350 kilometers, later redeemed by the Ministry of Railways, called the Guangshao section. During the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity diplomatic agreement in 1930, the National Government, recognizing the importance of completing the railway, decided to allocate all the indemnity funds to complete the project. The Ministry of Railways appointed Ling Zhuming, the former director of the Longhai Railway Engineering Bureau, to oversee the railway's construction. In the past three years, the 50-kilometer section from Shaozhou to Lechang will be completed in April of this year. As for the entire railway project, the most difficult section from Lechang to Dashimen has all the plans and designs ready and is scheduled to be put out for bid in March or April this year, with construction to begin soon. However, this section is very large, with seven tunnels within 45 kilometers, the longest reaching 230 meters, 250 bridges and culverts, the longest reaching 270 meters, over three million cubic meters of earthwork, and five to six hundred thousand cubic meters of concrete work. It is feared that only contractors with rich experience and strong capital can handle it. Knowing that there are many contractors in Shanghai with the above qualifications, it is planned to simultaneously solicit bids in Shanghai. The bidding advertisement has been entrusted to Shanghai architect Yang Ximiao by the bureau to distribute in Shanghai. It is heard that Chinese and foreign construction experts in Shanghai are paying close attention to the project due to the Boxer Indemnity guarantee and are actively preparing to participate in the bidding. Some have even personally visited the railway to inspect everything in order to accurately estimate the bid price, showing the importance construction professionals place on the railway project.

Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau Provides Shelter for Returned Unemployed Workers 130

Liu Qingquan Seeks Employment

The Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau recently received a letter from the Municipal Government Secretariat forwarding the case of Liu Qingquan, instructing the bureau to properly arrange for his resettlement. Upon inquiry, it was learned that Liu Qingquan is 47 years old, from Jinan, Shandong. He was a craftsman who went to France in 1916 under an agreement to work in the rear areas of the Allied forces. After the end of the European war, he continued to work in France to make a living. In recent years, he became unemployed and was repatriated by the Chinese Consulate in France. He presented various supporting documents, which were verified to be authentic. It was found that Liu Qingquan has considerable experience in machinery, ironwork, carpentry, and other labor-intensive jobs. He is also honest and diligent and has no bad habits. He is currently willing to seek employment in Shanghai to find a place to live and does not care about the wage. The Social Affairs Bureau, feeling pity for his plight, immediately sent him to the New Public Nursery for temporary shelter. Organizations or individuals in need of such a worker can contact the Fourth Section of the bureau at any time.

Assassin of Wu Guangzong 133

Defendants Suddenly Retract Previous Confessions in Court Yesterday

Judge to Issue Verdict Based on Previous Confessions

Wu Guangzong, the director of the Naval Survey Office, resided in the Ningkangli neighborhood of Ximen, Shanghai. Several thugs went to Wu's home last year. Wu was in the toilet at the time and was shot and killed. The concession police arrested five suspects, including Wu Jigui, Yang Sanmao, Zhang Shaoliang, Song Jiande, and Zhang Changlin, and transferred them to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation. After clarifying the situation, they were sent to the local court. The prosecutor investigated, and the defendants confessed to the shooting, citing Wu's harsh treatment of subordinates as the reason. The prosecutor then filed charges according to the law. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Shen held a court session. Unexpectedly, the defendants retracted their previous confessions, denying the act and refusing to explain the reason. The relatives of the deceased and witnesses identified Wu Jigui and Yang Sanmao as the ones who held and fired the guns. The judge, referring to the previous confessions and the witnesses' testimony, found the case clear and began the closing arguments, setting a date for the verdict. The defendants were remanded in custody.

Attempt to Smuggle Gold Bars 134

Valued at Two Hundred Thousand Taels

Confiscated in Full

The North China Daily News reports that before the departure of the Rutchputana on Tuesday, customs officers found five Chinese passengers in second class acting suspiciously, appearing to be carrying heavy objects. Request for Tax Exemption After New Oil Tax Increase 135

Since the Jianghai Customs implemented the increase in the import tax on petroleum on the 5th of last month, only the products of the Asiatic Petroleum Company, Standard Oil, and Texaco are exempt from the new tax. All other oil companies are required to pay the new tax on crude oil purchased from foreign countries. However, since the promulgation of the tax law, Jianghai Customs has not collected any of this new tax, but the refining industry has greatly declined as a result. The three major companies sell diesel to small refineries, raising prices by as much as 40 to 50 yuan above the market price. Refineries are severely affected by the high raw material prices and poor sales. Petroleum has a wide range of uses and is a necessary item for modern military equipment (as evidenced by the Russo-Japanese oil agreement to transport Russian oil to Japan for refining). The kerosene needed for today's machinery is very expensive, costing a huge amount of money each year. Now that China's industry is depressed, the authorities are not trying to save it, which concerns the people's livelihood and is no small matter. The US government exempts all raw materials that its country lacks from import duties. For example, tung oil is not produced in the US. Although the US government encourages planting, the output is still small, so it is exempt from tax when transported from China for sale. This is an example. It is heard that the Jiuji Oil Refinery and others in Shanghai have submitted a request to the Ministry of Finance for a tax exemption, which is expected to be approved.

Lai Yi Ferry Crossing Blocked 136

Merchants Petition for Retention and Opening

The Municipal Public Utilities Bureau's Eastern Route ferry has moved its dock from Lujia Ferry in Pudong to the Lan Ni Ferry Dongchang Road pier, starting yesterday. However, the Hongsheng Warehouse in the north blocked the privately-run Lai Yi Ferry crossing yesterday morning, and it was temporarily demolished after negotiations. However, the Pudong office of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce believes that the ferry crossing is an important passage for loading and unloading goods, so it has prepared a petition to the General Chamber of Commerce, requesting the Municipal Government to retain and open the ferry crossing to facilitate commerce. The original petition states: "The Lai Yi Ferry public ferry crossing has been suddenly blocked, causing public anger and a potential riot. We again request a speedy submission to the Municipal Government for an order to open the crossing. The Pudong Lan Ni Ferry crossing is the main route for the entry and exit of goods in the entire town. There is no other way. We previously heard that it would be blocked, and more than forty businesses, including the Rentai Rice Store, jointly requested assistance, and on the 4th of this month, we submitted a petition to your association requesting a speedy submission to the Municipal Government for relief. It has been half a month since then, and we have not received any instructions. This morning, the Hongsheng Warehouse suddenly blocked the ferry crossing by planting piles, causing the flow of goods between Pudong and the west to be cut off. The public is extremely angry and plans to organize a passive boycott to resist. We immediately went to various locations to persuade them to stop and wait for a solution and went to the Third District Bureau of the Public Security Bureau to meet with Director Zhang. Director Zhang agreed to persuade the compradore of the warehouse to temporarily remove the piles, and the manager was informed. The prosperity of commerce depends entirely on smooth flow and convenient transportation. Since the January 28th Shanghai Incident, all businesses have been depressed and operating in difficult circumstances, hoping for recovery. The ferry crossing is blocked, the source of goods is cut off, and the municipal ferry pier is only for pedestrians and does not allow the loading and unloading of goods. There is no other way out, and the stores will inevitably close their doors, turning the lively streets into dead alleys. Our Municipal Government is working hard to build and seek the revitalization of the entire city, and we believe that it will not regard Lai Yi Ferry as a lawless area. The situation is critical, and we are compelled to submit this petition to your association again, requesting a speedy submission to the Municipal Government to take into account the public interest and issue a clear order that the ferry crossing be open forever. Our 100,000 residents of the entire town pledge to be the government's backup and to deal with those who only care about their own interests. Respectfully submitted, awaiting orders with utmost urgency."

Junk Ship Crossing the Atlantic 139

| Departure from Wusong Yesterday |

Five Americans, including Bo Xuelou, purchased a three-masted junk (i.e., Ningbo fishing boat), named it "New Horizon", and embarked on the grand undertaking of crossing the Atlantic Ocean. The ship, originally named Jinbaoyuan, has a capacity of approximately 25 tons. It was initially docked at the Yunzaobang Estuary in Wusong for internal repairs. It is said that all the navigational equipment is complete, and there is an office and a wireless telephone installed. Two Chinese men, Li Yinhe and Wang Guiquan (both from Ningbo), were hired to handle the sails and steer the ship. Bo Xuelou gave each of them a settlement fee of 400 yuan. Yesterday morning at 12:00, the ship set sail from the Yunzaobang Estuary, embarking on a journey without a set timetable. Li Yinhe told reporters that the plan is to first go to Hong Kong and then cross the ocean. He said that the ship has been repaired and is sturdy, and there is enough food to supply seven people for more than a year. He only hopes that there will be no storms on the ocean surface so that they can reach their destination sooner, which would be very fortunate.

Engine Workers on the Jinghu Railway Refuse Pay Cut 141

Conflict in the Office

Zhong Yangqi Covered in Manure

The D-type locomotives of the Jinghu Railway Machinery Depot have a total of four engines, and the drivers and firemen are divided into eight shifts. When the locomotives are running, one shift is on the train, and the other shift is working in the engine room, taking turns. Recently, Deputy Engineer Zhong Yangqi proposed to reduce the number of D-type locomotive workers to six shifts to save money, but the workers demanded to maintain the status quo. Yesterday at 10:00 AM, a major conflict erupted in the office due to disagreement. During the conflict, someone in the crowd threw a bag of manure at Zhong, covering his body and the office with a foul smell. After the incident, Engine Room Director Li Xizhi arrived upon hearing the news, but the workers had dispersed. Realizing the seriousness of the matter and the difficulty of handling it, he immediately reported the matter to his superiors for review. The workers, on the other hand, felt that Zhong, as an engineer, should not have sworn at them. Last night, they gathered all the workers in the Longtou Room to discuss countermeasures.

Chai Sibao's Right Foot Bone Broken

An Englishman named Shi Meike (transliteration), 19 years old, residing at No. 303 Badang Road in the French Concession, was driving car No. 2166 yesterday morning around 10:00 AM when he suddenly hit and injured Chai Sibao, a nine-year-old girl and daughter of Chai Zhang, the owner of Zhengyi Stone Workshop on Hongqiao Road, knocking her to the ground. Police Chief Liu Gancheng from the police station arrived and took the offending car and driver Shi Meike to the station. Guo Weiyi Accused of Rape and Abandonment 143

| Hearing Postponed to Today |

Guo Weiyi, the owner of the Watson's Soda Factory at No. 327 Jiangxi Road, a Teochew native, 45 years old, residing at No. 23 Demingli, Pushi Road, French Concession, was recently sued in the Second Special District Court by a fellow Teochew woman, Lin Yayue (25 years old), represented by lawyers Wu Kai, Qu Xiaobai, and Ni Gangyi, in a criminal self-accusation of rape and abandonment, requesting an investigation and, in addition, a civil lawsuit seeking compensation of 61,568 yuan for living expenses, clothing, food, pocket money, labor costs, medical expenses, and interest on debts until the age of 60 for a total of 36 years. The gist of the lawsuit states that when the plaintiff was 15 years old in 1923, her mother arranged for her to be fostered at the defendant's home (then residing in Renheli, Songshan Road) and to sleep with his fourth son, A Qing. On June 17 of that year, at 2 or 3 PM, the defendant brought bathwater to the bathing room, offering to let the plaintiff bathe, and then closed the door, giving her a ring and coaxing her with sweet words. He then raped her. They cohabited for six years. Because the defendant feared his family's authority, he sent the plaintiff back to her mother's home in her hometown to protect his family harmony. Once separated, he did not communicate with her and abandoned her. When she came to Shanghai to find him, the defendant avoided meeting her, putting the plaintiff in a desperate situation. The court served the defendant with the lawsuit, and the defendant also retained lawyers Lu Shaozong, Yu Zhong, and Luo Er to file a defense, denying the rape, and filed a counterclaim accusing her of false accusation. The court originally scheduled the hearing for yesterday afternoon. Both parties and their lawyers arrived in court, and the defendant's family members also attended the hearing. However, due to the large number of cases, it was not heard until 6 PM, so the presiding judge, Xiong Huiping, announced that the hearing would be postponed to 2 PM this afternoon.

Anchor of British Queen Liner Recovered 144

Weighing 37 Tons, Valued at Tens of Thousands of Gold

The Changxing Company's world liner, the British Queen, lost one of its giant anchors, along with its chain, weighing a total of 37 tons when it arrived in Shanghai on the 17th of this month. The anchor's enormous size can be imagined. The anchor is worth tens of thousands of gold. The Changxing Company has been sending small boats and hiring sea divers to salvage it for days. After various difficulties, it has finally been recovered. It has now been decided that the recovered anchor will be transported directly from Shanghai to Japan because the British Queen is about to depart from Chunhuang Island to Japan. It will be reloaded onto the ship upon arrival.

Jiaxing Road Police Station Reassigned to Northern District 145

The Jiaxing Road Police Station of the Public Works Department of the Shanghai Municipal Council, formerly under the jurisdiction of District [D] (i.e., the Eastern District), will be reassigned to District [C] (i.e., the Northern District) starting from the first of next month. After this change, the police districts north of the Suzhou Creek will be divided as follows: The District [C] Chief's office is located in the Hongkou Police Station, telephone numbers 15380 or 42243. Its jurisdiction includes the Hongkou Police Station, West Hongkou Police Station, Dixwell Road Police Station, and Jiaxing Road Police Station. The District [D] Chief's office is located in the Wayside Police Station, telephone numbers 15380 or 52244. Its jurisdiction includes the Wayside Police Station, Yulin Road Police Station, and Yangtszepoo Police Station.

Henry & Co. Trading Company to Open Soon. In view of the rampant sale of counterfeit goods in the market, often disguised to resemble genuine products, and the high prices of European and American products, prominent figures in the local banking industry, such as Mr. Ye Xunruo and Mr. Li Dingshi, have pooled substantial capital to establish Henry & Co. Expansion of the Globe Brand Battery Factory. The Guohua Chemical Industry Factory on Huade Road in Shanghai, our country's largest battery manufacturer, exports Globe brand batteries, whose power and shelf life can rival imported products. A shelf life of up to one year, with a burn time of 16 hours, is a special feature of Globe brand batteries. Sales cover the entire country, and even overseas Chinese merchants often order by mail. General manager offices are located in major commercial ports. It is now heard that the factory's business has developed, and the original factory buildings are insufficient. A factory building has been built on the corner of Huade Road and Baoding Road, with a chemical laboratory, testing laboratory, and engineering department inside, using the latest scientific methods for production, all using the latest machines. There are more than one hundred male and female workers, producing one thousand dozen Globe brand batteries every day, yet there is still a shortage.

Establishment of the China Parts United Transportation Branch. The China Overseas Department Store Parts United Transportation Branch at 3 Ma Road, Shanghai, has been established because stores and firms have always had difficulty transporting parts and goods. Due to the lack of a formal organization or postal restrictions, they have been forced to transport goods privately, and there have been reports of merchants suffering losses due to customs inspections, fines, and confiscation. In view of this situation, the branch has submitted a report to the Ministry of Industry of the National Government for approval and registration, and the Jianghai Customs has issued a special permit to transport parts nationwide in order to meet the urgent needs of society and protect the interests of merchants. The branch has now printed ten thousand copies of transportation instructions for merchants and firms to request and read.

Famous Architect Dies 153

Mr. Qiqi Hudec, the brother of Mr. Lazlo Hudec, a famous architect in Shanghai, has been in Shanghai for many years, assisting his brother in painting and architecture as his right-hand man. Recently, he has been painstakingly planning the 22-story building of the Four Banks Joint Savings Society for his brother, sparing no effort. As a result, he contracted enteritis and was admitted to Baolong Hospital for treatment, but the treatment was ineffective and he died in the hospital at noon yesterday. It is heard that he will be buried in the Wanguo Cemetery on Jingansi Road at 5:03 p.m. today. All his friends and acquaintances, upon hearing this bad news, mourn his loss.

Tenants of Hengfeng Lane Oppose Rent Increase 154

The tenants of Hengfeng Lane on Shigaota Road, North Sichuan Road, Shanghai, are opposing the unreasonable rent increase by the landlord. The tenants of the entire lane have held several meetings and unanimously believe that the area, including Zhabei, has suffered heavy losses due to the January 28th Incident, and the market is depressed and has not yet recovered. The landlords of the houses near the area have all reduced rents to show sympathy to the tenants, but the landlord of this lane not only refuses to reduce the rent but even increases it by as much as seven yuan. Although the tenants have repeatedly objected, all to no avail. Therefore, the tenants of the lane have now submitted a petition to the municipal government requesting a ruling.

Reader Advisor 159

Why Don't Young People Like to Read?

丨丨A letter from Mr. Guo Zizhen of Tanggu丨丨

Dear Reporter: Many difficult questions in the "[Reader Advisor]" column have been solved by you, and I now have a question that I would like to ask you to think about carefully and explain in detail. I am very grateful. I often hear that many young people cannot study because of poor family conditions, and I have never heard of anyone who is provided for but refuses to study deeply, but my brother is such a person. He has parents, two older brothers, and one older sister, and one younger brother. The older siblings have all received higher education, and the father and eldest brother are all working far away in Xinjiang Province. He is sixteen years old this year and graduated from Beijing Municipal Middle School last summer. He took the high school entrance exam twice but failed to pass both times. I am very worried about him, but I am working outside and cannot teach him every day, so I repeatedly wrote to him, telling him not to be discouraged and to prepare hard for the exam this summer, as he is still young. Sometimes when I go home, I earnestly tell him that a person must have rich common sense in order to make a living in the future, and this common sense must be obtained from books during the student days. I have cited many examples of famous people who suffered many hardships in their youth and later made amazing contributions to the country and society, and he agrees very much. But as soon as I leave, there are only his mother and his sister, who is still studying, at home, and he just doesn't listen to their teaching. He is restless and doesn't review his books. He feels that there is no fun in the family. Once he even joined the army on his own initiative, but after some effort, he was sent home again. He wrote to me saying that he was willing to work and study part-time, or to find him a job. I knew that he didn't want to study, so I didn't find him a job. I always hope that he can take advantage of the time when he is being provided for to obtain higher knowledge, or to learn a specialized skill, so that he can do something big in the future, so I advise him to cherish his youth, put in some hard work, and seek true advice, so that he will not have to worry about having nothing to do in the future, but he still doesn't seem to be aware! I am now asking you to answer the following points on my behalf: (1) His environment allows him to study, so why does he feel that studying is not interesting and want to find a job? (I have read the article in the "Shen Bao Monthly" about the problem of youth boredom). (2) How can I make him change his mentality of seeking a job and continue his studies? (3) Is it possible to allow his request and find him a job? I hope that you will take the trouble to answer the above three points on my behalf. (Reply will be published tomorrow)

Important News 160

The China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture

Business Will Cease

Affected by Deferred Payment of the Boxer Indemnity

(Beijing, 23rd) Ren Hongjun, the Director-General of the China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture, stated that the foundation's self-operated and subsidized educational and cultural undertakings depend on the Boxer Indemnity for support. Last year, due to the suspension of the payment of the Boxer Indemnity, the operating expenses of various undertakings were borrowed from various banks and are urgently needed to be repaid. If the payment is suspended again this year, various undertakings will inevitably cease. The Boxer Indemnity that the foundation should receive is only more than 2 million yuan in national currency, which is very small for the government.

National Boy Scouts Donate to Purchase Aircraft 161

丨Provisionally Set Donation at 100,000 Yuan丨

March 1st to August 31st

Comrades in the Boy Scout community across the country, in view of the fact that modern self-defense weapons, especially aircraft, are the most powerful, and that if our Fifth Army, the 19th Route Army, had adequate aircraft to confront the enemy during the January 28th Incident, we would have been able to leave not even a single Japanese soldier behind, have suggested to the preparatory office of the National Boy Scouts of China and Vice President Dai Jitao to donate funds to purchase aircraft for the country to strengthen national defense. The General Assembly believes that this suggestion is indeed important and has passed the measures at the second preparatory meeting, which will be distributed to the party headquarters and councils of various provinces and cities for serious implementation by the national Boy Scout groups. The measures are recorded below:

Measures A. Every Boy Scout donates at least two copper coins per day for six months. B. Every service member donates at least one yuan per month for six months. C. Every group donates at least two yuan per month for six months. D. The donation period is from March 1st to August 31st. E. The donation is reported by each group to the General Assembly once a month, and the General Assembly will deposit it in the bank. F. The donation is kept by a designated staff member of the General Assembly. G. The donation is provisionally set at 100,000 yuan. H. The purchased aircraft is named "[China Boy Scout No. ○]". I. In addition to the regular donation, service members and Boy Scouts may donate a special donation. J. Service members who donate a special donation of 20 yuan or more and Boy Scouts who donate a special donation of 10 yuan or more will be given a commemorative certificate as a token of appreciation. According to statistics, there are currently 760 Boy Scout groups, 3,905 service members, and 61,031 Boy Scouts in the country. The amount of donation is expected to be at least 100,000 yuan, which will be a small contribution to air defense equipment. 162

Japanese Ministry of Education to Issue Mobilization Order 165

Starting March 1st, a Four-Part Mobilization to Promote a Major War

(Tokyo Hualian, 22nd dispatch) The Japanese Ministry of Education held a departmental meeting today. Minister Hatoyama stated that after the League of Nations passes the advisory, Japan will withdraw from the League of Nations. The international situation will therefore undergo major changes, and the domestic morale will inevitably be affected. If preparations are not made early, it will inevitably lead to internal changes. All division chiefs and section chiefs expressed their opinions, stating that the opportunity must be seized to encourage national unity against foreign forces to prevent anomalies. All educational institutions will be mobilized, starting from March 1st, to begin work. It is reported that the mobilization methods decided by the Ministry of Education are as follows:

(1) The first step is to mobilize the 8 million-member male and female youth corps.

(2) The second step is to mobilize the 4 million-member National Women's Federation to encourage the 20 million housewives nationwide to rise up and sacrifice for the country. (3) The third step is to mobilize the teachers and staff of national primary schools and the Boy Scouts.

(4) Finally, mobilize the 2 million-member youth military training institute.

In the above order, they will proceed in four parts, organizing national lobbying teams, film crews, and document propaganda teams, etc., and are scheduled to complete the first phase of work from March 1st to the end of April, it is said.

George Bernard Shaw's Remarks in Peiping 166

Are Old Relics of the Imperial Palace More Important Than People's Lives?

Chinese Students Studying Communist Theories is Problematic

Why Bother Interviewing Me on Japanese Matters?

(Special Dispatch from Peiping) British literary giant George Bernard Shaw, who participated in the greatly beneficial around-the-world tour group, left Qinhuangdao on the Beining special train at 7:00 AM on the 20th, amid cheers from the crowd. He arrived in Peiping at 6:40 PM that evening. Accompanying him were over 130 male and female members of the world tour group. When the train arrived at the station, Shaw resided in compartment number 3, with his silvery beard shining brightly under the lights. A crowd gathered outside the train, vying to see his demeanor. Soon, Shaw, accompanied by his wife and attendants, alighted from the train. Shaw was wearing a light green raincoat, carrying two small leather cases, a camera, and a large leather briefcase. His wife was also carrying a fashionable large leather briefcase. After alighting, the receptionists sent by Zhang Xueliang, acting chairman of the Peiping Branch of the Military Affairs Commission, rushed forward to carry Shaw's belongings, but Shaw repeatedly said "No, no." He strode forward briskly, hand in hand with his wife, out of the station. At the same time, the members of the tour group also disembarked from the train one after another. Previously, the Pacific Railway Company had booked 80 rooms at the Beijing Hotel and arranged for over 60 cars to wait at the station. They immediately boarded the cars and went to the Beijing Hotel on East Chang'an Street to rest. Shaw stayed in room 305. Twenty-two Chinese and foreign reporters submitted their cards requesting to see him. Shaw, feeling tired from the journey, apologized to the reporters and introduced Miss Gaolun, secretary-general of the tour group, to discuss the time for the meeting. It was then agreed to meet at the ballroom of the Beijing Hotel at 9:00 AM on the 21st. At 9:10 AM on the 21st, seventeen Chinese and foreign reporters visited Shaw and were received in the ballroom of the Beijing Hotel, where he made the following remarks.

Shaw's Remarks on Chinese Culture 167

I came to Peiping solely for sightseeing and to visit the world's famous ancient capital, with no other mission or purpose. Reports say the Sino-Japanese issue is serious, and Rehe is particularly tense, with Peiping and Tianjin also being in a dangerous zone in the future. My coming to China and traveling around during China's serious situation is different from the impressions of Europeans coming to China at ordinary times. Peiping is a magnificent and opulent old capital. If countries do not forget China, they should not forget Peiping. Japanese residents are preparing to return to their country, as if a great disaster is imminent. Chinese rich people are also moving south, as if Peiping can be abandoned. The property of the rich must not suffer the slightest loss. I don't understand what this means. Is the property of the rich more valuable than Peiping? The southward transportation of cultural relics from the Forbidden City adds a page to the cultural history of Peiping, as if the antiques are more important than the lives of millions of Peiping people. If we go to Italy to travel, all the antiquities from the Roman era still exist. I have never heard of Italy moving cultural relics east or west due to foreign aggression or internal strife. The Chinese people love peace. The Japanese also claim to love peace. But the peace the Japanese talk about is the peace after the result of war. The Chinese peace is peace within peace. Now the Japanese have declared to the League of Nations that the protection of Manchuria is their responsibility, and the invasion of Rehe is to protect the screen of Manchuria. They make aggressive invasion under the name of protection, regarding it as [self-defense]. China adopted a policy of non-resistance, and now they feel that the policy of non-resistance is not applicable, and they are changing to a policy of resistance, also regarding resistance as [self-defense]. I don't know when the self-defense movements of China and Japan will end. Some young Chinese students are interested in communist theories. Although the government has repeatedly ordered against it, the student elements are still complex. Communism is a political issue, but originally it was an economic issue. Now it has changed into a political issue. Whether communism is right or wrong is still a question worth studying. Russia first failed because it adopted absolute communism, and then changed to the New Economic Policy and implemented the Five-Year Plan. Now this plan has been declared successful. China is not easy to spread communist theories, and China does not have large capitalists. The issue of labor and capital is not yet a question for the Chinese academic community to study, so whether communist theories have power in China is not something I am happy to talk about. A few years ago, Beijing prohibited students from studying the Three People's Principles. After Peiping was settled, Peiping regarded students studying the Three People's Principles as good students, so whether a theory is right or wrong is entirely [time-bound,] not permanent. As for my sightseeing, I believe that Chinese monuments are unique historical materials in the world and have immense value in cultural history, he said.

Busy Sightseeing, No Visits to Song and Zhang 168

When Shaw met with reporters, he did not recognize the seventeen reporters. After the explanation, he laughed and said, "Why bother interviewing me on Japanese matters? I came to Peiping for sightseeing and have no mission." When the reporters were leaving, a Russian reporter suddenly came, claiming to be a reporter stationed in Peiping for a certain newspaper. Shaw said, "[You are late. Students are deducted points for being late. Reporters who are late get no news.]" The Russian reporter said, "[Please forgive me.]" Shaw laughed and said, "[I am not a teacher, and it is not that I don't want to talk to you more, but because time is short,] please forgive me." At this point, reporters asked Shaw when he would visit Song Ziwen and Zhang Xueliang. Shaw replied that Mr. Song was busy with politics and finance, and he was busy visiting ancient monuments and famous scenic spots. Mr. Zhang had political knowledge and was clear about the international situation. His courageous spirit was reminiscent of his father. It was a pity that Mr. Zhang Zuolin was killed by the Japanese and could not save China from danger at this time. Because he was busy with sightseeing, he was afraid he would not be able to visit Mr. Zhang Xueliang. As for the academic community in Peiping, who invited him to banquets, he could only thank them. At this point, Shaw shook hands with the reporters and said goodbye.

Rejection of Tianjin Students' Welcome 169

The British Empress of China ship arrived in Qinhuangdao from Shanghai late on the 19th. Because it was late at night, all the members of the tour group stayed on the ship overnight. The Beining Railway was ordered to specially prepare a special train, which was parked at the East Station of Qinhuangdao Wharf. At 10:30 AM on the 20th, all the members of the tour group left Qinhuangdao by special train to Peiping. At 3:00 PM in the afternoon, they passed through Tianjin. George Bernard Shaw was sitting in the third compartment of the fourth carriage. Teachers, students, and newspaper reporters from Tianjin Beiyang Institute of Technology, Nankai University, and the Chinese and Western Girls' School boarded the train, crowding into the carriage to express their welcome to Shaw. Unexpectedly, Shaw ordered the porter to lock the compartment. All the welcome personnel came excitedly and returned disappointed.

The Local Municipal Bureau of Education Obeys Orders to Strictly Instruct 171

Various Middle Schools to Improve Teaching and Training Management

The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education yesterday instructed the principals of middle schools in the city, stating, "According to Order No. 1261 of the Ministry of Education, a review of the results of the recent middle school student graduation examinations in various provinces and cities shows that a large number of students failed. This is due to the uneven level of students, but the poor management and teaching of schools in peacetime are also a major cause. When students first enter school, there is not much difference in their academic ability. If the managers can pay close attention to teaching and guidance in peacetime, students will progress gradually, and their grades can at least reach the minimum standard. However, most middle schools today follow old ways in teaching, neglect training and management, and pay little attention to checking academic performance in peacetime. Or, the selection of teaching materials is inappropriate, or teachers and teaching materials are changed frequently, and there is no connection between them, all of which can lead to a decline in academic level. Since this examination, the management performance of middle schools in various places has been clearly revealed. In addition to the grades of each school having been announced by the relevant departments in accordance with Article 11 of the Provisional Regulations for Middle and Primary School Student Graduation Examinations, the relevant departments should immediately investigate the number of students taking the examination in each school. If more than half of the students fail, the relevant departments should give each school a warning or rectification depending on the circumstances, ordering them to improve teaching and management. If the results of the next examination still do not improve, all public and private middle schools should be given more severe sanctions or closed down, so that the teaching efficiency of middle schools can gradually increase and live up to the state's aim of running schools and educating talents. This is our high hope." We hereby order all schools to be informed.

The Municipal Bureau of Education Urges New Students, etc. to Submit Enrollment Forms Today 172

The Municipal Bureau of Education yesterday instructed the following schools: Shanghai Municipal Yangjing Junior High School, China Women's Physical Education Normal School, Liangjiang Women's Physical Education Normal School, Southeast Women's Physical Education Normal School, Chinese and Western Women's Middle School, Zhirenyong Women's Middle School, and Guangzhao Junior High School, stating, "According to regulations, middle schools in this city should fill out enrollment forms with the qualifications of new students and transfer students at the beginning of each semester, and submit them to the Bureau for review together with supporting documents. This Bureau has repeatedly issued official documents ordering compliance and issued enrollment forms in Order No. 475 of the first semester of this year, ordering immediate completion and reporting on record. Your school has not complied with the order to submit the form for the first semester of this year, which is negligence. We hereby order you to urge again, limiting you to ten days from the date of this document to promptly comply with the previous order, fill out the first semester enrollment forms completely, and submit them to the Bureau for review together with each student's supporting documents. If there is a delay in filling out and reporting, all graduation certificates of students graduating from your school in the future will not be stamped because the enrollment cannot be verified. You are hereby informed."
