Football Friendly Match: Yu You Clashes with British Soldiers 176

Result: 10 to 1

Yu You's Refreshed Lineup Shows Considerable Strength

The Yu You football team recruited new players and underwent rigorous reorganization, aiming to restore its former renowned reputation. Li Shiyou from Hong Kong, whose arrival in Shanghai had been publicized for a long time, has joined Yu You, revitalizing their lineup. This Sunday, Yu You will face a strong opponent, Noakes, at the Chinese baseball field. To consolidate their lineup and prepare for the upcoming battle, they arranged a friendly match yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM against the British Army RASC (Royal Army Service Corps – Specialist Volunteers) stationed in Shanghai at the Chinese baseball field. More than two thousand fans, eager to witness the new lineup, attended as spectators. The match resulted in a decisive 10-1 victory for Yu You. Their performance was remarkable. Li Shiyou's right wing proved to be an excellent addition. Throughout the game, the British Army was consistently under Yu You's pressure. Were it not for Wang Caigao's "own goal," the entire British team would have been utterly defeated.

Four Consecutive Goals 177

The two teams faced off, exchanging attacks for several rounds. Li Shiyou unleashed his speed on the east side, penetrating deep into the defense. With a cross pass, Chen Guangyao received the ball, sending it towards the goal. Hu Youcheng slid in, opening the scoring. After the restart, Sun Jinshun, taking advantage of an unguarded moment, launched a solo attack, scoring a goal. Soon after, Sun’s foot again penetrated the enemy's territory. Li Shiyou assisted by hooking the ball, sending it in lightly for another goal. The momentum of Yu You was overwhelming. The British soldiers desperately defended, panting rapidly. Sun Jinshun dribbled straight ahead, and Xi Qiaosheng emerged as a hidden force, scoring another goal.

[P Losing a Goal>

The Navy, conceding four goals in a short period, were filled with indignation and launched a retaliatory offensive.

They charged several times, but the defense led by Lao Xie (nicknamed Old Crab) Rao Huisheng and Xiao Xie (nicknamed Little Crab) Ye Jinming was impenetrable. The left wing, Lat, evaded Shi Jinsheng and charged past Rao Huisheng. Bao Nai lifted his foot to kick the ball away, but Wang Caigao crouched down hoping to save it, but unexpectedly, Ha Yin arrived, bouncing the ball off Ha Yin's body and rolling it into the net.

Three More Goals Scored 178

At this time, Yu You's momentum was unstoppable. Their forwards were remarkably fierce and brave. Sun Jinshun repeatedly launched attacks, once dribbling straight up to the 25-yard mark and shooting from afar, achieving a remarkable goal. Li Shiyou launched another attack from the flank, rushing to the line and sending a beautiful cross to the goal. The "locomotive" Chen Guangyao arrived and headed the ball into the net. Five minutes before halftime, Sun Jinshun scored another goal, making the score 7-1 at halftime.

Not Seeking More 179

The second half began, and the British army's strength was waning.

Their play was disorganized. Only Yu You's players were seen running everywhere. Li Shiyou opened the scoring from 15 yards out, followed by Hu Youcheng's charge for another goal, and Xi Qiaosheng smoothly added another, making it ten. Yu You was content and didn't seek more goals, so the game became less intense and less exciting, not worth elaborating.

Page 12

Chunqiu (Spring and Autumn)

Refuting the Absurd Claim that China Has No Culture 185

— Xu Ruhui

On the 18th of this month, the newspaper reported that the British playwright and literary figure George Bernard Shaw arrived in Shanghai from Guangdong, and the city's celebrities, journalists, academics, and artists gave him a warm welcome. After landing, he went to the World Society, where he was met by Mei Lanfang for a discussion. Shaw's tone was quite sharp, and Mei was unable to effectively counter his arguments. Shaw criticized Chinese opera for having noisy percussion, and Mei replied that while Peking opera had such noises, Kunqu opera did not. This response was clearly a retreat, acknowledging the flaws of Peking opera. Couldn't Shaw have countered that Kunqu also has percussion? I don't know how Mei would have answered that. It was like a fight where there was no exchange of blows, so Shaw made the statement that China has no culture. I don't know if Shaw was referring to Mei personally or to China as a whole. I want to tell Shaw that percussion originated in China during the Tang dynasty and was often used in ensemble with string and wind instruments. During the Jiaqing era of the Qing dynasty, a set of "ten-part music" was added to the imperial banquet music. There were ten sizes of gongs and more than a dozen sizes of drums. The surviving scores contain eighteen sets, with four main categories of sounds: wind, string, plucked, and percussion. The instruments are numerous, and the percussion instruments create complex and harmonious sounds, vastly different from ordinary folk music. Also, historical records from the Tang dynasty state that Emperor Ming of Tang himself conducted a large musical performance in the garden using a kettledrum, causing all the flowers to bloom, which shows the value of percussion. I hope that Shaw will not make such incomplete arguments in the future, and I also hope that Mei will read more ancient books and conduct fundamental research, and not boast about his thirty years of theatrical life, because performers thirty years ago were mostly uneducated and lacked skill. Their qualifications and status cannot be compared to those of today's performers. Doesn't Mei know this? I say this not only for Mei's sake, but for the sake of all those who bear the responsibility of culture. As for rural culture, Shaw did not specify what its state is, which is puzzling. So, where does China's true culture lie? Four thousand years ago, there was a specific term called "sound education" (also known as ritual and music), which encompassed everything from national ceremonies to social interactions, as well as scholars reciting, vendors doing business, and even beggars begging for food. Shaw's so-called "natural culture" is likely to be found here, not elsewhere.

Eating 186

— Chi Fo

丨Nothing in the world is as difficult as eating丨

Eating is both the most difficult and the easiest thing. Why is it the most difficult? As the ancients have already said, "Nothing in the world is as difficult as eating," which is a golden saying. Why is it the easiest? With specific reasons, eating becomes the easiest thing. For example, newborn babies and old people nearing their end, who doesn't know how to eat? So eating is the easiest thing in the world, that is irrefutable proof.

The theory of relativity of eating has already been established today. Look at the officials in government, the staff in large stores, and various agencies. Who isn't holding a position, carrying a rubber rice bowl, and eating until their faces are round like Wuxi clay figurines? If you check their resumes, they are not graduates from prestigious universities, but rather the little brothers of concubines or the uncles of respected ladies. Family connections are naturally more powerful than any graduation diploma.

The methods of eating are ever-changing. The skill of holding a rice bowl is infinitely subtle and can only be truly understood and mastered by the individual, and cannot be described by my humble pen. In short, the art of eating is more important and wonderful than any other art. Unless you are friends who practice abstinence from grains and consume only air, who can afford not to explore the art of eating! After all, we Chinese people have studied the art of eating thoroughly. Even if our stomachs are narrow, the more rice bowls, the better. Holding only one bowl in hand is not enough to satisfy us. We might as well reach out and snatch other people's bowls. One bowl, two bowls, three bowls, four bowls... as long as we are full, caring about other people's hunger is foolish.

In my hometown, there is a custom where beggars barge into restaurants. After eating their fill but unable to pay, they simply kneel respectfully on the street for an hour or two, and then they can leave without trouble. Some people laugh at them, but in reality, most people in the world only have food to eat if they kneel. There is no need to laugh at the beggars! In the past, a fallen nobleman was said to have begged for food with a golden rice bowl, which was considered a joke. In fact, many modern youths suffer from this problem, which is truly lamentable.

Mysterious Transactions 187

— Rong Yu

丨One of Society's Ailments丨

"Use my money to exchange for your goods." This is the fundamental principle of trade, which is such a just and open thing. Look at the many large corporations with neon lights and banners proclaiming great discounts, and every one of them is thronged with people. Even the vendors selling peanuts, carrying small bamboo baskets and raising their voices like bamboo poles, have many customers. They are openly buying and selling, and no one can deny that. However, in Shanghai society, perhaps because it is overly civilized, there are many transactions that have a mysterious air about them. If you don't believe me, look at the following examples!

During the day or night, if you happen to walk along North Sichuan Road, especially the area where Qujiang Road borders the Chinese and foreign concessions, you will see many men in short clothes standing near the utility poles. They are wearing peaked caps at an angle. In a Chinese-style jacket with a Western suit jacket, they are densely stationed like sentries. When they see young men, especially sailors from warships, they stick close behind you, muttering, "Western miss, Japanese miss, beautiful looks, cheap prices, you can choose whatever you want."

As you walk south along Sichuan Road, reaching the famous Fourth Road (Fuzhou Road), you will always see many dark-skinned, shabbily dressed old men standing under the eaves. If you call them beggars, they don't ask you for money. If you call them vendors, they aren't carrying any goods. However, as long as someone walking by glances at them, they will come forward, listing a whole series of Western "girls" and Japanese nude photos. They will even tug at your sleeve and ask you to go into the alley to look at samples.

As you continue walking south and enter the French Concession, you will pass through several famous alleys, such as Baoyu Lane. If you are well-dressed and look energetic, someone will come up to you and ask, "Sir, the tables are open again, would you like to go have some fun?" If you look darker and more dejected, then another type of person will greet you with a different pitch: "Sir! Cold medicine for relief, clean rooms, four coppers a box."

These are all transactions, but they are furtive and carry a mysterious air about them. They fully demonstrate the decadence of society. Now, let me add two more types of transactions: one is the forced sale of human flesh, and the other is the habit of selling without buying. These two are also quite peculiar and mysterious. If you walk along a busy road at night, and if you are dressed in a rural style, I guarantee that you will be surrounded by prostitutes selling flesh and poison. They will use a forced rape-like and enticing method to drag you in. Even if you don't want to do anything, they will still force you to spend a few cents before you can escape. Whether on walls or utility poles, you will find a few crooked and slanted red papers, especially in winter. These are advertisements for selling treatment for severe colds. I think this kind of transaction is only one-sided. If someone were to buy it, it would be a great joke and make people laugh their heads off!

Recently, the water shortage problem has caused an uproar in the city. Analyzing the root cause, the water from the water company comes from the Huangpu River, which belongs to China and costs nothing. Now, the company is arbitrarily raising prices and forcibly cutting off the water supply. Therefore, I ask the water company respectfully about the "tap water":

"Where does the water come from?"

The Landlord 189

— Qin Shouou

"Third Son! Come over and see Brother Zhao off!" Another group of people poured out from the back room, all in short clothes and narrow trousers, bareheaded, wearing boots, each holding a weapon, some with spears, some with single-edged swords, and two children about ten years old mixed in. Everyone was smiling, walking excitedly onto the square. The spirit of ancient Chinese warriors was still fully preserved here!

As soon as the landlord finished shouting, a middle-aged man in his forties threw down his weapon and ran over.

"Brother Zhao! Don't say such things!" The Third Son had already taken his father's place in supporting Brother Zhao. "Haha! What's the use of money? You're sick and can't work. We should be giving you more money, not talking about owing it. Brother, if you need money, just send your wife over to ask for it! We have rice too! Everyone in the village is family, why distinguish between you and me? Haha! Goodbye! Forgive me for not seeing you off!"

"You treat us too well, Landlord!" Brother Zhao clasped his fists, tears streaming down his face.

"Take care of your health!" The landlord sighed deeply, turned around, and stepped quickly into the ranks of the warriors.

The sounds of shouts and swords clashed with the roaring of the six fierce dogs. They immediately felt ashamed and dropped their golden, silk-like tails, scattering in six directions out of the woods. Only the mangy dog remained lying in the shadow of the setting sun, continuing to admire his masters' military exercises.

"Little Ling! Why can't you ever get it right?" The landlord straddled a huge stone lock as if riding a horse, with his broadsword planted in front of him, the breeze blowing and his long beard constantly brushing against the hilt. The one being scolded was his grandson, a twelve-year-old boy. Little Ling was using a long spear. Probably because he didn't have enough strength, the spear often fell from his hands when he sparred with others. Because of this, the landlord was quite annoyed that he wasn't working hard enough. (2)

"Perform it again! How can you fight the Japanese like this?" Little Ling's father, the landlord's second son, also felt that Little Ling was letting him down. He flicked Little Ling on the forehead, ordering him to perform again alone, and at the same time using the shocking words "Japanese devils" to motivate him. (2)

World News

The Glass Rooms of Paris 190

— Feng

Almost everyone knows what "glass rooms" are. In Paris, they exist on almost every street corner. They have no other identification except for stained-glass windows and a scarlet door light, which burns all day and night, emitting a dazzling ray of light.

They are the public brothels of Paris. The prostitutes inside are, of course, different from those who stand guard on the streets. Among them, there are also ranks, depending on the quality of the brothel. However, they all have one thing in common: cleanliness and hygiene. They must be inspected twice a week by the health bureau, and those with diseases can no longer stay in the brothel to entertain guests. Therefore, customers no longer run the risk of contracting diseases.

When you press the door button, the bell inside rings "ding-dong, ding-dong". A hostess immediately leads the visitor into a room. Inside, there is a row of standing prostitutes. They are all nude, allowing visitors to appreciate their beautiful bodily curves. Once he has made his selection, she leads him to a bedroom. Regardless of the brothel's quality, the rooms are all elegantly and beautifully furnished. Sanitary equipment is all available.

Hygiene is also something they pay close attention to, so they inevitably examine or wash the guests. Here, there is no such thing as emotion, only sexual desire. However, the length of stay varies. The more money given, the longer the stay. Overnight stays are also possible. Both long and short stays have fixed prices, with no deception. A short stay is fifteen minutes and costs about fifteen francs (equivalent to three Chinese dollars), which is the price for an ordinary brothel. A more expensive one costs more than fifty francs (ten dollars or so). The reason why these brothels are expensive is partly because the prostitutes inside are younger and more beautiful, and partly because the furnishings inside are particularly exquisite.

The establishment of glass rooms has many benefits: hygiene, simplicity, and satisfying men's sexual desires. These are all essential elements for preserving national health.

A Young Man's Troubles 191

— Dong

He is an eighteen-year-old youth. He has beautifully shaped eyebrows and very bright eyes. His teeth are not perfectly aligned, but they are very white. Tall stature, solid skin. All together, he is undoubtedly a handsome man.

He has money; studying at a certain university in Shanghai costs several hundred dollars a year. Therefore, in terms of material possessions and academics, he feels satisfied. He has never shown any unhappy emotions. On the ship returning from abroad, he sometimes meditated alone on the deck, sometimes chatted with a young woman in the officer's cabin. Although his appearance was always smiling, his heart revealed an unspeakable melancholy. One day, his secret was revealed to me by a third party. It turned out that he was a young man with marital worries. His father had arranged a marriage for him when he was not yet five years old. Because he had grown up in Southeast Asia, he had not yet met his fiancée. But according to information gathered from various sources, she was neither attractive nor had she attended school. Therefore, this young man's mind was often filled with the serious question of whether or not to marry her.

Needless to say, his body and mind had been baptized by modernism. Marrying a woman he did not know and had no feelings for, wouldn't that conflict with modernism? At the same time, wouldn't that endanger his lifelong happiness? But how could he not marry her? His family had already issued two or three ultimata, saying that if he did not marry the woman they had arranged for him, they would resort to force. The so-called forced method was to cut off his financial support.

Under this threat, the young man was truly embarrassed. Furthermore, the woman's family repeatedly urged them to get married, which made him feel that his dark future was drawing closer day by day. He considered this problem for three days. Finally, he said to me with a resolute attitude: "Mr. So-and-so, this time when I go back, I will definitely find a way to see that woman. If she's good, I'll marry her. If not, I'll have to find another way, and maybe I'll have to ask you for advice again."

Free Talk

Grasping Several Important Issues 192

— Yang Qiu

The Japanese imperialists have launched another all-out offensive on Jehol. This fact is not surprising, because in essence, it is only a continuation and expansion of the aggression and atrocities of the September 18th Incident in the Northeast, and it is inevitable given the military and political perspectives that the Japanese imperialists will not allow Jehol to remain under the setting sun. What should we do about this continued and expanded aggression? Our answer is: resist, fight, wash away blood with blood, and give back tooth for tooth!

However, there are several problems standing in the way that we must firmly grasp!

First, the significance of this struggle cannot be sought solely from empty terms such as "nation" or "ethnicity," but should be based on the larger topic of "anti-imperialism" and its historical mission. Our weapon is a "national revolutionary war," and our goal is to "overthrow imperialism!" This struggle is not only for the liberation of our nation, but for the entire world, for the future of history. Second, launching a national revolutionary war naturally requires the formation of a broad "national united front" and total mobilization of the entire nation. But we also recognize that those who are severely oppressed have a stronger will to resist and greater fighting power, so we believe that in the current national revolutionary struggle against Japanese imperialism, we must not neglect the help of the most oppressed "laboring masses."

Third, since the Nineteenth Committee passed the entire draft report, perhaps many people could not help but cheer and celebrate, believing that this was a "victory of justice" and "international assistance." In reality, if we do not deliberately ignore the fact that the British ambassador to Washington, Lindbergh, proposed to the US State Department that Singapore be used as a US naval base in exchange for war debt negotiations and an economic conference, and the fact that Washington is actively promoting war debt negotiations and an economic conference, then we can see that the League of Nations' attitude towards Japan has suddenly become slightly more assertive, entirely due to war debt negotiations. People are calculating their own interests, but we think it is a "victory of justice." This kind of mistaken understanding is as base, shallow, and meaningless as begging the League of Nations for help!

Grasping the three important issues mentioned above, grasping the weapon of national revolutionary struggle, is necessary; otherwise, we will not know why we are fighting and why we are dying!

Letter from the Countryside near City L 193

— Ms. Wang Wanrong

Dear Jie:

I arrived in City L safely yesterday and spent the night at my aunt's house in the city. This morning, I took off my cheongsam, removed my scarf, put on the blue cloth gown my aunt had prepared for me, and put on a woolen hat. Looking in the mirror, ah! Jie! I really look like a complete country youth! You know, if I didn't disguise myself like this, I wouldn't be able to go home. I would be taken to the mountains by bandits halfway there.

My home is more than fifty li from City L. I set off at seven in the morning and arrived home a little after twelve o'clock. Walking quickly, I didn't feel cold. Unfortunately, the snow on the road melted slowly in the sunlight. Wearing the pair of worn leather shoes my cousin lent me, it was really difficult to walk. Otherwise, I could have arrived home an hour earlier!

You all go home to enjoy family happiness, to be spoiled by your mother, and to set off firecrackers with your younger brothers. What about me? I have no parents, who can I be spoiled by? I also have no innocent younger siblings, only two imposing older brothers. I have several nephews too, although they are all under ten years old, they all know how to shoot guns. This time when I go home, there's really no joy at all!

As soon as you open the door here, there is a mountain. There are wolves on the mountain. Listening to the wolves howl while lying in bed at night is the most interesting thing. When going up the mountain, rabbits often run down. When I see them, I chase them. They perk up their ears, their ruby-like eyes twinkling as they run into the woods. If I get angry, I just need to take the gun off my shoulder, aim, and bang!

Then there would be a delicious rabbit to eat that day. But I really can't bear to use such vicious methods on such lively and lovely little animals, ah! It would be better to just kill someone!

This year is considered peaceful. There haven't been any major incidents in this area recently. We should be able to have a peaceful New Year. Let me tell you about some of my past life experiences: The houses here all have high black walls and six or seven large doors. When I was five years old, a large group of bandits surrounded my house. My father knew he was outnumbered, so he opened all the doors and said loudly, "Anyone with courage, please come in!" The bandits thought there must be some kind of defense inside, so they all quietly slipped away. Little did they know, my father was singing an empty fort strategy!

One night four or five years ago, I was awakened by a burst of barking. I quietly peeked outside through a crack in the window. Ah! It was terrible! A large group of bandits had come again, holding bright torches in their hands. I woke up my older brothers and sisters-in-law (my parents had already passed away at that time), and we held our guns and shot down through the window slits. The bandits also fired back. Bullets whizzed over our heads. As a result of this fierce battle, four bandits were killed. I can't remember who killed them. The rest all ran away. The next morning, when I looked in the mirror, it was terrible! A large patch of hair on top of my head was burnt!

Another year, I was studying in the city! Many bandits had set up camp near our village and often came out to rob houses. My eldest brother and many villagers fought with them. As a result, my eldest brother was captured. The bandits wanted us to redeem him with 50,000 yuan early the next morning. Where would we get so much money? That night, the whole family decided to fight the bandits. Actually, everyone knew in their hearts that not only would we not be able to rescue my eldest brother, but we might all die in the hands of the bandits. But none of us said a word of timidity. After walking a short distance, we saw a red glow in the distance, and the sound of shouting and killing. At first, we thought the bandits were prepared. When we got closer, we realized that the bandits were fighting with the security team from another village. My eldest brother was lying deep in the woods, moaning. Jie! It turned out that the bandits saw the security team going to attack them. They thought they were going to rescue my eldest brother, so they stabbed my eldest brother a few times and left him to fight. That's why my eldest brother was lying in the woods, moaning. The next morning, the bandits had all fled. We went to see the bandits' residence. In the large manor house, there were more than a hundred cotton quilts and a dozen water buffaloes left behind. Since then, the bandits haven't visited for a long time. My aunt has repeatedly advised us to move into the city, but my sister-in-law can't bear to leave those high mountains, those streams, those peach trees, those taro fields. As for me? I also think we shouldn't be too timid and let the bandits occupy this beautiful village for nothing.

I really can't get used to life at school. The Suzhou girl at the same table always laughs at my large appetite. One day, when we were studying sociology, we went to visit a model prison. On the way, we encountered a horse walking alone. The girls who trembled even when they saw dogs fighting were all terrified. I found it funny, so I went up and held the horse. Only then did they tiptoe past. They were really pitifully and laughably weak!

It's a pity there are no bandits this year. Otherwise, I would definitely ask you to come and stay here for a few days. Although you are also delicate, you like bravery and strength. Didn't you say to me at school? ["Yu! Have you eaten enough? Don't starve and lose strength, so you won't have the strength to kill bandits when you go back."] Jie, now I haven't lost weight, and my strength is still the same. But it's a pity there are no bandits to kill!

I can't get used to living in my old home. When the weather gets a little warmer, I'll come out again. Goodbye! Your friend, Yu. January 16, 1933.

The Story of the Black Woman Seeking God (10) 194

— By Xiao Boner, Translated by Xuanxian

"Climb down that tree, you look frightened," the black girl said.

"This is really an interesting thing," the nearsighted man said, now that he felt safe, he calmed down. "This is a conditioned response. I wonder if I could make a dog climb a tree?"

"Why would you want to do that?" the black girl said.

"Well, to make this phenomenon have a scientific basis," he said.

"Nonsense!" the black girl said. "Dogs can't climb trees."

"If there hadn't been the imagined carp stimulus, I wouldn't have climbed either," the professor said. "How can I make a dog imagine a carp?"

"Introduce him to a few real carp first," the black girl said.

"That's very expensive," the nearsighted man said, frowning. "Dogs are cheap, if you buy them from dog thieves, or buy a batch when dog taxes are levied. Buying carp would cost a lot of money. I have to think carefully about it."

"Before you go," the black girl said. "Tell me, do you believe in God?"

"God is an abandoned and useless assumption," the nearsighted man said. "The universe is just a huge system of reactions produced by vibrations. If I tap you on the thigh, your knee will definitely shake."

"Then I'll tap you with my Nobel Carey; you better not do that," the black girl said.

"For scientific purposes, it is necessary to restrain the subject and prevent such obviously inappropriate subordinate reactions," the professor said. "But as examples of reactions produced by association, these are also quite appropriate. I have spent twenty-five years studying the effects of such reactions."

"Effects on what?" the black girl said.

"On the saliva of dogs," the nearsighted man said.

"Considered to be relatively intelligent?" she said.

"I am not interested in intelligence," he replied. "In fact, I don't know what it means, and there is no reason to believe it exists. My business is in learning things that people have never known before. I convey that knowledge to the world, thereby contributing to the collective of definite scientific truths."

"When the world is full of knowledge and no kindness, how much better will the world be?" the black girl said. "Don't you have enough brains to think of some appropriate way to discover the things you want to know?"

Remembering Wu Lake 195

— Zhenfu

Since the spring breeze blew away the cold snowflakes, bringing wisps of fine rain, I can't help but think of the spring in my hometown, and remember Wu Lake. Wu Lake, although it is not as beautiful as West Lake, nor as vast as Tai Lake, its tranquility and simplicity have their own charm that makes people linger; moreover, it is my old friend of more than twenty years, my only comforter in lonely times.

Wu Lake is about thirty li northwest of the Oriental Grand Port planned and built by Mr. Sun Yat-sen. It only has simple clothes and a kind smile. If you can't stand the intense stimulation in the city, if you are tired of the sounds of cars, trams, carriages, and all other machinery, or if you feel that you have contracted the urban illness of neurasthenia, then you can appreciate the tranquil beauty of a place like Wu Lake.

What embellishes Wu Lake and adds to its beauty are the willows in the park and the five-story pagoda east of the lake. In the past, the park was called Parrot Island. Was it because it was surrounded by Wu Lake water and adorned with fragrant grass? Actually, I have never seen the shadow of a parrot there. Is it always because of the Tang poet's line "Fragrant grass lush on Parrot Island"? It made it get this irrelevant noun. In fact, this is also the habit of our compatriots. Don't you see the signs of "Rice Fragrance Village" everywhere? As if without such an elegant noun, it would be dull and colorless. The park being called Parrot Island is just a manifestation of this mentality.

At Wu Lake, we can appreciate the slow return of spring. When the fragrant grass on the ground gradually turns green, and the willow branches gradually turn tender yellow, spring is reporting its slow return here. Birds are playing welcome songs, willows are waving welcome flags, and the lake water is also showing a welcoming smile. Everything is welcoming the arrival of spring.

The best time is on a moonlit night, sailing a small boat, with one or two close friends, rowing oars, and swimming in Wu Lake. Wu Lake is generally round, and the moon in the sky is printed into the heart of the lake, reflecting each other, a piece of silver light, decorating the entire lake surface. When the oars are rowed to the center of the lake, it is really like breaking the bright moon in the water, the silver light is dazzling, and we almost suspect that we have rowed into the Milky Way. The willow branches brush the silver light, dancing gently, the thin clouds floating faintly, the shadow of the pagoda in the southeast can be vaguely identified, this is really a beautiful and quiet scene. Sometimes there is no moon, and dots of stars fill the sky. If you are afraid of the danger of rowing a small boat, then you might as well go to the park for a walk, look at the calm lake water, like a mirror, reflecting the dots of starlight, like pearls, like jewels, like thousands of points of affectionate tears, sprinkled all over the sky. On the grass, you can sit and lie down, listen to the faint singing of the lake water, and the conversation between the willow branches and the wind. Here, you can appreciate the secrets of nature, you can indulge in the embrace of nature, you can forget all your worries and depression. There is no urban noise here, and no ugliness of modern society.

Spring has returned to the human world. At Wu Lake, the willow branches may have changed from light yellow to tender green, and the lake water may still contain a faint smile. In Shanghai on this rainy night, I can't help but think of you. I wonder if, when the willow branches are dancing, the birds are singing, and the lake waves are smiling, welcoming the return of spring, can dear Wu Lake remember its old friend hundreds of miles away thinking of you?

American Subsidiary Coin Committee 204

Passes Bill to Prepare for Silver Purchase

Reuters Washington, 22nd: Today, the House Auxiliary Coin Committee passed a proposal, which would order the U.S. Treasury Department to buy $250 million in silver in preparation for silver subsidiary coins. A kind of silver subsidiary coin coupon will be issued for this preparation. The silver purchase procedure, the first three months purchase price is limited to four corners and one ounce, the second three months high price is limited to five corners and one ounce, the third three months high price is limited to six corners, from then on, the treasury purchase price can be increased by half a point per ounce per month, until it is increased to seven corners and five points one ounce.

Securities 212

Public Bonds Under Pressure from Both Bulls and Bears

Short Covering Drives Recent Surge

Yesterday, trading on the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange for public bonds was quite chaotic due to it being the last day of the month. Amidst the ongoing fighting in Jehol, prices struggled to rise due to short covering for the current month. During the morning's initial trading, demobilization bonds rose sharply, reaching a peak of 30.05 yuan. Afterward, price increases were more moderate. Bonds near the 20th issue mark saw gradual decreases of 0.12 to 0.2 yuan, while salt tax bonds rose by 0.15 yuan. This unstable situation was caused by the intense struggle between bulls and bears this month. In the afternoon's initial trading, most bonds from previous issues retreated by 0.2 to 0.3 yuan, while consolidated salt tax bonds rose again by about 0.1 to 0.2 yuan. The chaotic situation had truly exceeded the norm, with the trend seemingly dictated by the ups and downs of consolidated salt tax bonds. Although rumors were rampant after the opening in the afternoon, short covering remained aggressive. Northern bankers and retail investors were especially busy, pushing prices up several jiao. Bonds from the 19th issue saw a wild surge of 1 yuan this month, while consolidated salt tax bonds only rose by 0.2 to 0.3 yuan. As a result, the situation changed again at closing. Demobilization and troop reduction bonds, which had already risen by 0.2 to 0.3 yuan this month, fell again by 0.25 yuan as Northern bankers sold off forward contracts. Therefore, most bonds that followed were weak, and salt tax bonds were especially sluggish, with both current and next month's contracts falling by 0.4 to 0.5 yuan. Trading was dominated by retail investors, with large players making few moves. Northern bankers were relatively busy. As a result of the market prices, bonds from the 18th issue and earlier fell by 1.5 yuan due to the large price gap. Spot demobilization bonds, which had not been actively traded recently, also fell by 1.5 yuan. The remaining futures contracts generally rose, with demobilization bonds for the current month rising by 1.8 yuan, and bonds from the 19th issue rising by 1.45 yuan. The rest only rose by 0.2 to 0.6 yuan, while salt tax bonds only rose by 0.05 yuan. The total trading volume was 9,708,000 yuan, including only 3,000 yuan in spot trades, with consolidated salt tax bonds accounting for 4,000,000 yuan, and demobilization bonds accounting for 1,500,000 yuan. The remaining bonds each accounted for several hundred thousand. Today's futures trading will only be for the month of March.

Erratic Yarn Market 214

The yarn market was weak in the morning and strong in the afternoon, with an erratic trend. The fact is that a portion of investors, with a small capital base, were preparing to hoard for a long time, and many were bullish. Therefore, the buying sentiment rose again when the market fell slightly. However, sellers, considering the urgent national crisis and their abundant inventories, tended to short sell. Therefore, the competition between bulls and bears was intense. However, the Yunnan and Sichuan merchants are currently purchasing spot yarn, which greatly stabilizes the buyers. If the demand continues steadily, the market may see a rebound of 200 to 300 taels. The biggest key lies in real sales.

The Russians believe that Japan's refusal to sign a non-aggression treaty with Russia is shocking. The newspaper replied that Soviet Russia is committed to peace and does not want to interfere in the battles of imperialist countries. The troops are constantly arming themselves and preparing to extend their murderous hands to the borders of Soviet Russia. British Man Kills Wife

Claims Suicide

Already Detained by the British Municipal Council

(Tianjin) An Englishman, Hicks, has been in China for more than 30 years. During the Guangxu reign of the Qing Dynasty, he married a Chinese woman in Guangzhou and had three daughters in a row. Hicks was displeased and married a woman surnamed Lai in Hong Kong. Later, they came to Tianjin together. He worked in customs for more than 20 years, accumulated 1 to 2 million yuan, and then resigned. On the night of the 22nd, he suddenly shot and killed Lai in his residence at No. 35 Hong Kong Road. He placed the pistol in the deceased's left hand and calmly went to the British Municipal Council to report that his wife had committed suicide. On the morning of the 22nd, the British Municipal Council sent someone to examine the body and found that the direction in which the deceased's left hand held the gun did not match, which was obviously a murder. He was immediately detained. On the morning of the 24th, the British consul interrogated him. Hicks insisted that it was suicide but could not provide any evidence of suicide. The British consul scheduled to examine the body again on the afternoon of the 24th to determine whether he had been murdered. According to Lai's parents, Lai married Hicks at the age of sixteen and is now thirty-nine years old. At first, Hicks falsely claimed that he had no wife, so Lai rode in a bridal sedan. Later, she learned that he was a bigamist. Hicks was lustful and recently placed a maid in Beiping. Hicks often molested her, and Lai tried to dissuade him. Hicks became angry out of shame and turned into anger, and now this tragedy has occurred. (Special dispatch, 24th)

South African Federation Organizes Mixed Government 264

Reuters telegram from Zhen, 23rd General Herzog, the Prime Minister of the South African Federation, has formed a trial method with General Smuts, the leader of the opposition party, to organize a mixed government. This is the most important development in South African politics in recent years. According to this agreement, Herzog will still be the head of the new government, but Smuts will also have an important position. The new agreement stipulates the dissolution of the parliament and does not submit a budget bill. The parliament will probably be dissolved in the middle of next week, and the budget bill will be the work of the new parliament. The general election is scheduled to be held in May, so the new parliament will be convened in about July. The political opinions of the two major political parties in South Africa are usually very different. The compromise reached by the leaders of the two parties is limited to broad principles. As for the cabinet positions, they have not yet been effectively distributed. The agreement also stipulates that the status of South Africa as part of the British Empire will be fully maintained, and there are also regulations on the indigenous people's problem, which has been in dispute in the past. Both Herzog's National Party and Smuts's South African Party are scheduled to hold political party meetings tomorrow. It is expected that this agreement can be passed.

League of Nations General Assembly Agenda Today 269

Future Focus Will Shift to the Rehe Situation

Our Representative Will Ask the Assembly to Deal with It Conscientiously

The Nineteen Special Committee Advocates Expanding the Restructuring to Invite the U.S. and Russia to Participate

(Geneva) There will be a very important development when the League of Nations General Assembly meets on Friday. Its agenda has been agreed upon by the Nineteen Special Committee this afternoon. Chairman Hymans will deliver the opening speech at 10:30 tomorrow morning, explaining that he speaks on behalf of the entire Nineteen Special Committee, so other special committees will not speak again. After the Chairman's speech, the Japanese representative Matsuoka will be invited to speak. At that time, there will be a dramatic scene. Matsuoka will definitely announce Japan's position on "Manchukuo" in very strong terms, pointing out that the Rehe incident is an internal affair of "Manchukuo." Matsuoka may also blame the League of Nations for causing the crisis. It is also unknown. It is expected that Matsuoka will leave the meeting place before the vote without participating in the Nineteen Special Committee. Representatives who have not participated in the Nineteen Special Committee, such as the representatives of Venezuela, Lithuania, and Canada, will express their opinions one after another after Matsuoka's speech, but they all agree to keep their speeches brief. After everyone's speech, the vote will be taken. Then, Chinese representative Yan Huiquing will address the General Assembly, detailing the current situation, and especially on Rehe, there will be earnest remarks, asking the League of Nations how to deal with it well, so as to prevent repeated aggression. Then, the League of Nations General Assembly will ask the Nineteen Special Committee to propose measures to prevent repeated aggression, and discuss it at the next League of Nations General Assembly. The next General Assembly will be held on Saturday. It is heard that the Nineteen Special Committee advocates organizing another committee according to Article 3 of the League of Nations Covenant, which will be composed of twenty-one people, that is, the representatives of Canada and the Netherlands will be added to the former Nineteen Special Committee. However, it is also expected that some new people will join. Hymans has now explicitly stated that although he is willing for Belgium to have a representative to attend the twenty-one-member committee, he cannot participate in the future committee. This committee, when it is established in the future, will act on behalf of the League of Nations General Assembly. This is not a negotiation committee, because the negotiation committee can only be established after both parties accept the report. If a negotiation committee is established, the League of Nations will ask Russia and the United States to join, but the Nineteen Special Committee has also carefully considered the possibility of inviting Russia and the United States to participate in the twenty-one-member committee, feeling that it is easier to get the two countries to cooperate with the new committee than to ask them to join the Fifteen Special Committee. This is also one of the reasons why the Nineteen Committee plans to change to the Twenty-one Committee. This afternoon, before the adjournment, the Nineteen Special Committee reviewed and approved the opening and closing speeches that Chairman Hymans will deliver at the League of Nations General Assembly on Friday. (Reuters dispatch, 23rd)

Japan's Mandate Issue after Leaving the League of Nations 272

Germany Advocates Return of Territory 273

According to the Tokyo Nichi Nichi Shimbun, if Japan withdraws from the League of Nations, the German Hitler cabinet will advocate for the complete return of the South Pacific mandate territories to Germany. The League of Nations also has the same idea. However, this claim was originally intended to alleviate the feelings of the German people regarding the issue of arms reduction. Currently, the German foreign authorities and influential figures are still unwilling to publicly discuss this issue. Dr. Huesner, a well-known colonial policy expert and former member of the investigative committee, has also not expressed his opinion. However, the general view of the German representatives is to take back the territories because Germany has no base in the East. If this territory is taken back, it will have a significant impact on Japan's military. Although Japan withdraws from the League of Nations, it will never easily give up its mandate over the South Pacific. Germany's strong desire to reclaim it will inevitably lead to conflict with Japan. At a time when Japan and the United States are facing off militarily, if Germany insists on demanding this territory, it will inevitably be drawn into the vortex. Therefore, recently, discussions on this issue have been raging in Germany.

Recent Developments in Soviet Urban Development - Moscow Correspondence 274

Striving to Build, Rapid Population Growth

Cities and Villages Becoming Integrated

Since 1917, the development of Soviet cities can be divided into two periods: the first from 1917 to 1922, when people fled to the countryside due to food shortages and industrial decline; and the second from 1923 onwards, when industry developed, and cities flourished even more by 1926.

In 1921, the Soviet urban population suddenly decreased from 20 million to 16 million. This was the era of the Russian Revolution, when the entire country was surrounded by armed intervention from various countries and the White Army of the Tsar. All efforts were devoted to the struggle for survival. Due to a lack of raw materials, the total industrial output in 1920 was only 18% of the output in 1913, and the number of workers in industry had decreased to 43%. Excluding the Black Earth Belt (the main agricultural area of Russia), the urban population shrank by more than 35% between 1916 and 1920. The situation was even more severe in the central region. In other regions, the reduction was more than 27%. The population of St. Petersburg lost 62% from 1910 to 1920, returning to the level of half a century ago. Moscow reached the level of 1897. Moscow lost 175,000 residents, Leningrad lost 1.5 million, Baku lost 40,000, Dnipropetrovsk lost 50,000, Kharkov lost 25,000, Stalingrad lost 48,000, Samara lost 74,000, and Nizhny Novgorod lost 57,000.

In these years, Tashkent and other agricultural areas absorbed the people who fled from the cities, and the population in the countryside increased by 60% to 80% from 1917 to 1919.

At the same time, the number of workers in large industries also decreased sharply, from 2,599,000 in 1913 to 1,585,000 in 1920. The 30 provinces of Great Russia saw a reduction of 30%. Moscow saw a reduction of 48% from August 1918 to July 1920.

In recent years, large industrial centers in the Soviet Union have experienced unprecedented development and prosperity. The number of cities with a population of over 100,000 has exploded, and medium-sized cities with a population of 20,000 to 40,000 are also growing rapidly. Most people are increasingly attracted to industry, and many cities in the Soviet Union are not only not lagging behind the pace of urban development in Europe and the United States, but are surpassing it.

For example, Detroit, the large center of the American automobile industry, only increased its residents by about five times in the 27 years from 1900 to 1927. In contrast, Stalingrad, the Soviet Detroit, more than doubled its population in just five years. Nizhny Novgorod (now renamed Gorky) increased its population by about four times in eleven years. Essen, the center of the German coal mining industry, only tripled its population in the 20 years from 1901 to 1920. In contrast, Shchëkino in the Soviet Union increased its population by six times in just eight years (from 1923 to 1931). During the same period, Makeyevka increased tenfold. Lyon, the large center of the French textile industry, only increased its population by one-fifth in the 26 years from 1900 to 1926. In contrast, Ivanovo in the Soviet Union increased its population by three times in eleven years.

If we do not talk about general figures, but examine individual cities, then the development of new Soviet cities is even more obvious. Here are a few examples to illustrate the general situation:

Novosibirsk During the World War, the city's 275

commercial turnover totaled 86 million rubles, and freight totaled 1 million tons. The main enterprises were flour milling, winemaking, and leather making. The two iron-making enterprises each had only 128 workers. In 1913, the city had a total of 21 industrial enterprises, with 1,138 workers and a total output of 8,359,000 rubles. In the four years of the first five-year plan, the city's industrial output increased by 600%, from 25 million to 154 million (by the end of 1932) rubles. The number of workers increased from 2,600 to 10,800, an increase of more than 400%. The average output per worker increased by 50%. The city has now decided to build a large integrated factory for manufacturing mining machinery (this factory started construction in 1931 and will be completed in 1934).

(Part of it,) a large factory for manufacturing textile machinery, and other large enterprises. The city now has 235,000 residents, compared to only 65,000 in 1913. It has five commercial vocational schools with 2,500 students, 29 scientific research institutions, 29 periodicals, 65 kindergartens, 26 nurseries, and 18 clubs. All other modern facilities, such as running water, mechanical laundries, cooking factories, new large residences, and wide streets, are being constructed one after another.

Karaganda 276

Before the revolution, the city was leased to the British for coal mining, and two or three worker dormitories were built. In the nomadic steppes of the Cossacks, there were only two or three small villages with 4,000 to 5,000 residents. But by 1930, the city had become the third largest coal industry center in the Soviet Union, with an annual output of 700,000 tons of coal. The population suddenly increased to more than 100,000, including 40,000 cadres. In 1931, the city was equipped with hospitals, clubs, power plants, and radio stations. During the second five-year plan, the city decided to develop into a new socialist city.

Almaty 277

The capital of Kazakhstan, in the past this city was a concentrated city of local tyrants and bureaucrats. In the meantime, the number of residents has tripled (50,000 in 1929, increasing to 150,000 in 1931). The city's cultural and economic construction plan budget for 1932 reached 45 million rubles, of which housing expenses accounted for 7.5 million, administrative agency construction expenses reached 9.5 million rubles, industrial expenses accounted for about 6 million, cultural and educational expenses accounted for 8.2 million rubles, health expenses 1.5 million, and public welfare expenses 3.5 million rubles.

Luhansk 278

In 1910, the city had a total of 24,000 residents. Now it has increased to 170,000. It is estimated that in 1933, the construction of new factories and workers' quarters will increase by 20,000. The Soviet Union's new modern railway locomotive manufacturing plant, which ranks second in the world, is located in this city. There is a long list of such rapidly developing new modern cities in the Soviet Union. Due to space limitations, only a brief mention is possible. However, from the above-mentioned places, one can imagine the development of other places.

Overall, from 1926 to 1932, the percentage increase in the industrial population of various national republics was as follows: Russia, 217.5; Ukraine, 153.6; Uzbekistan (only Tashkent), 259; Turkmenistan, 211. The development of Soviet industry, considering the previous backwardness of various national republics, and the average distribution of industry throughout the federation, resulted in such a widespread and rapid increase in the industrial population of various national republics. In the Tsarist era, the proportion of municipal expenditures compared to national expenditures was the lowest in the world. In the United Kingdom, this proportion was 90%, in Denmark, 87.2%, in Switzerland, 68.5%, and in Russia, only 8.5%. Even in this meager amount, the amount used in remote areas of various ethnic groups was even smaller. In the Tsarist era, the municipal facilities of Ukraine, the so-called most advanced, had running water before the European War, but its main city, Kiev, according to the chairman of the city council, Joseph, said in a speech at the first congress of representatives of the whole city in 1913, that the city's electricity and trams were only enjoyed by the [middle] class, to put it bluntly, by rich people. [I have never seen a small house with electric lights. I have never seen a worker on the tram]. However, in today's Soviet Union, major constructions such as running water, sewers, trams, and electric lights are all set up in workers' areas. With the development of industry, a whole new city has been created.

In the past four years, the total investment in public welfare undertakings in the Soviet Union has reached approximately 20 billion rubles, and the construction cost of new housing has reached 35 billion rubles.

Compared with those before January 1 of the same year, the new houses added at the end of 1932 increased by 95% in Nizhny Tagil, 90% in Kuznetsk, 83% in Shakhty, 80% in Berezniki, 70.7% in Chelyabinsk, and 40% in Novosibirsk.

On the other hand, we see that the residents in the centers of large cities in Western Europe are sharply reduced, and almost all housing construction has completely stopped. A large number of unemployed people have moved out of their homes because they cannot afford to pay the rent.

The compilation of the second five-year plan is guided by the principle of eliminating the opposition between cities and villages, that is, determining [the future industrial development] route of national construction, and creating new industrial centers in rural areas, so that the differences between cities and villages can be gradually eliminated.

Under this policy, not only has industrial construction been evenly distributed according to the national region, but also on the basis of state-owned farms and collective farms, machine tractor stations have been widely established in rural areas, becoming the center for the implementation of agricultural mechanization.

Therefore, during the second five-year plan period, due to the expansion and development of the machine tractor station network, the widespread and in-depth agricultural mechanization, and the large-scale construction of industry in backward areas, the distinction between cities and villages will be eliminated in the Soviet Union.

National Salvation Bonds 286

Japan Implements

Industrial Immigration Plan

The Second Step in Annexing Manchurian Enterprises

The Tokyo Hochi Shimbun reports that since the implementation of agricultural self-defense immigration groups, various important undertakings have gradually shown signs of prosperity due to the concrete development of Manchurian-Mongolian economy. Now, they are further implementing the second step of the immigration policy, which is to establish an industrial immigration group plan. Currently, the Kwantung Army Special Service Department and the South Manchuria Railway Economic Investigation Committee have conducted a detailed investigation into the industrial aspects, and the specific proposal has been agreed upon as follows: (1) In Manchurian enterprises with a monopolistic nature, those that usually employ more than 100 office workers and employees should have half of their employees be Japanese. (2) Starting from this year, with three years as a period, 10,000 industrial immigrants (including families) (approximately 30,000 to 50,000 people) will be transferred to Manchuria and distributed to existing, unestablished, and newly established enterprise organizations. (3) The necessary travel expenses for this immigration will be entirely borne by the entrepreneurs. (4) The Japanese government will bear a portion of the various facilities necessary for the immigration group, such as education, hygiene, and security. In this way, not only can the surplus labor force in Japan be distributed, but also the industries of the entire Manchuria can be developed.

You Tiao (Fried Dough Sticks) 296

— A Tang

Today, after reading Mr. Yiran's article "[Sweet Fermented Rice]" in this publication, I immediately thought of "[You Tiao]."

The manufacturing methods of things like "[Sweet Fermented Rice]" and "[You Tiao]" were, of course, secretly groped out by predecessors and are definitely not based on any scientific knowledge. However, we can now discover that the manufacturing of these things demonstrates very interesting chemical principles, which shows the importance of the relationship between chemistry and daily life.

Now, let's talk about the manufacturing method of you tiao and the chemical principles involved.

First, prepare a bowl of cold clear water, about 400 cubic centimeters. Dissolve 5 qian of fine alum powder in the water, then add 3 qian of baking soda and 2.5 qian of table salt. Stir with a stick until completely dissolved. At this time, many bubbles will form in the bowl. Blow away the bubbles, and the water in the bowl will turn milky white. This water is what makes the you tiao expand and become hollow. Now, let's write the chemical reaction equations below:

(1) The chemical reaction of alum and water:

２Ａ１Ｋ（ＳＯ４＋Ｈ２Ｏ２Ａ１ＯＨ）３Ｋ

２ＳＯ４３Ｈ２ＳＯ４

Alum Water Light Aluminum Hydroxide Potassium Sulfate Sulfuric Acid

(2) After adding baking soda, it reacts with sulfuric acid. The formula is as follows:

３Ｈ２ＳＯ４ＳＨＮSHNaCO3　3NA2SO46

H2O　6CO2

Sulfuric Acid Baking Soda Sodium Sulfate Water Carbon Dioxide Now we need to do the second step: mix this water with 4 liang of fine wheat flour and continuously knead it into a paste with your hands. When you pick it up with both hands, the wheat flour paste should be able to leak through your fingers. Then, transfer it to a board, stretch it into a strip shape, about 7 centimeters wide, then use a knife to cut it into small strips. Stack two small strips together, gently press them with a bamboo tube, then stretch them out and twist them into a spiral strip. Place them in a hot oil pan, and wait for them to expand and turn golden brown, then the you tiao is done.

When the you tiao is placed in the oil for frying, the carbon dioxide gas contained in the batter is subjected to intense heat, and its volume expands. At this time, the small powder on the outside of the you tiao turns into dextrin and combines with the gluten, preventing the carbon dioxide gas inside from leaking out. Therefore, the you tiao expands under the pressure of the carbon dioxide gas.

As for the light aluminum hydroxide, potassium sulfate, and sodium sulfate, these things all remain in the you tiao, but these are all non-toxic. You can eat you tiao with peace of mind.

Literature and Art

Miscellaneous Thoughts on Liaodong 297

— He Shouren

I once heard of naval vessels stationed in Bohai (During the Qing Dynasty, Daoguang and Xianfeng eras)

During the years when the Anglo-French allied forces attacked Tianjin and Dagukou (There were troops stationed in Lushun and Dalian), it was a time when the Central Plains was filled with the sound of drums and war cries (It was the time of the Taiping Rebellion). They dared to boast that the nine border garrisons had fierce warriors (Since the Republic of China, the three northeastern provinces have increased their military strength year by year to two or three hundred thousand soldiers). Who knew that a sudden whale roar would occur (The September 18th Incident). Burning oneself has a reason because of one's teeth, Indulging the enemy, one regrets biting the navel for no reason. Ashamed of becoming a puppet monkey, Pitifully, the borders are touched like sheep and goats,

The Xiongnu often wanted to peek at the grazing horses, The Northern Expedition's carriages and horses left the border. The painted horn sounded, and the star banner moved in the wind, The snow pressed down on the yak tail standard, and the feathered urgent dispatch sped away. Fortunately, the Treaty of Nerchinsk was successfully concluded, Spreading out the map, I feel the boundary marker has been moved, Even the full flourish of the past was like this, Today's perilous situation is easily known, The Longsha road is long and far, For ten years, I have followed the army and the captive's spirit has disappeared, People think of Ban Chao for expanding the territory, Who can be entrusted with planning the border like Huo Qubing, Everyone passed on that the Flying General could subdue tigers, I don't believe that barbarian chieftains dare to shoot eagles, How can I bear to let the rocky border be ruined and embroidered, Do not say that the strong enemy is the favored one of heaven,

War Front Letters 298

— Wen Huan

Goodbye, a temporary goodbye from the last bitter kiss! It's pitiful to say, growing up in a metropolis, I have never been a sojourner in a foreign land; this time, for the sake of the country's survival and the nation's life, I have come to this bitterly cold northern land for the first time. When I was little, I often heard my father say: how cold the north is, how difficult it is, now I have finally experienced everything firsthand. Since last winter, it has been snowing heavily every day, and the mountains, fields, and villages are all immersed in a silver world. The cold weather is often more than ten degrees below zero Fahrenheit, and frostbite is common. Many brothers have been taken away by death due to their inability to adapt to the climate. "[How many people have returned from ancient battles]," it is indeed meaningful. However, we have now completely forgotten our own survival, our own physical bodies, and have long dedicated them to the god of life. Death seems to have nothing to do with us. We are constantly preparing for death, death, death, sacrificing death for the liberation of the entire Chinese nation is glorious and great.

Now our military supplies have been replenished, and we have arrived at a certain place on the front line from the rear defense. In recent days, the entire front line has been unusually silent, with only small contacts between the sentries of the two sides, and enemy iron birds constantly coming and going in the sky above us for reconnaissance. Other than that, there is nothing happening, it is simply hard for us to believe that this is a battlefield. Everyone in the deep trenches is very happy every day, there is talking, there is laughter, and the ringing radio also sends out pleasant songs from time to time, like a prelude to the war, celebrating our victory. Bang bang bang… Puff puff puff… The enemy has launched a general attack. A burst of battle cries, a burst of gunfire, followed by a burst of hand-to-hand combat. God, please give us this time! We are waiting with full willingness.

X, my best person, the person I love the most, please rest assured! Those who are destined to die will definitely not die. Those who live in a drunken dream, not resisting, may not be visited by death. China is now in danger of death at any time and anywhere, natural disasters can kill, the Communists can kill, warlord infighting can kill, imperialist aggression can kill, nowhere are we not in the teasing of death. Instead of watching the country change color and the volunteer army being defeated one by one, it is better to come to the front line happily and fight the enemy to the death with our flesh and blood. Our heads are worth an enemy bullet. You must do your best to maintain the affairs of the family! Our time together was really too short. A big gap will inevitably form in each other's hearts. However, we who have dedicated ourselves to the liberation of the country and the nation can only take the love of the entire country and the entire nation as our object, and fight and sacrifice. Our souls have deeply merged into the great soul of the entire nation. We are now striving for a life of love for the entire nation, and we are willing to charge into battle with the spirit of praying for death. X, please bless us! The war situation is critical, so I will stop writing here. Wishing you health! Your X at the very front line of Jehol

Our Way Out 299

— Mi Er

At a time when all industries are depressed, the economy is in panic, strong neighbors are pressing, and people's hearts are treacherous, we [young people] constantly feel the difficulty of finding a "[way out]." It's like Wu Zixu losing his way in the mountains when he hadn't passed Zhaoguan. But at that time, there were still people who could clearly point out his way out. But what about us? No matter how we shout and cry, who will pay attention to us? From this point of view, our situation is indeed much more difficult than Wu Zixu's! In other words, our situation is like "[running a horse on the bow of a boat, there is] no way out!"

Indeed, many young people feel pain and disappointment because of job or economic problems. Some feel pessimistic because of the approaching foreign invasion and the difficulty of the country's future. Some, although they have jobs, feel that their positions cannot be permanent, and therefore feel depressed. Some, although they have jobs, are oppressed by the "[Fifth Class]," and therefore feel resentment. Finally, and most commonly, they fall into decadence because of broken love.

The above-mentioned kinds are, of course, the depression of the average young person [excluding a few]. Even the author himself has experienced many of the various joys and sorrows, and has spent a lot of time objectively considering what he has encountered from beginning to end. The final result [— no, it is also our lesson —] tells me: apart from striving to work hard to change my own situation, there is really no second "[way out]!"

Let me give an example. For example, if my lover leaves me, of course I will feel frustrated at first, but my conclusion is: I should work hard to increase my knowledge, and work even harder to forge my physique, and find a partner who suits me better in the future! Sometimes, when I encounter the situation of being oppressed by the "[Fifth Class]," of course I will feel angry at first, but the conclusion is: work hard! Study hard! When my talent and intelligence reach a considerable level and I can find a considerable position, I will leave without regard for anything!

In short, in the course of our lives, every disappointment, frustration, and indignation is an opportunity for us to strive for progress! Perhaps some people think this is completely idealistic. In fact, no! Because the author himself, after coming out of the third grade of elementary school, encountered the above-mentioned misfortunes, and every time he didn't use this to stimulate his ambition, and every time he was not successful. After leaving the third grade of elementary school, I entered the business world, from an apprentice in the accounting room, to a telephone operator, to a junior high school teacher, to a senior high school teacher. In recent years, I have been working as a translator in an international organization.

Finally, I must also declare that in the course of my progress, I have not received the pity of philanthropists, the help of big figures, the comfort of lovers, or the promotion of relatives. In other words, it is entirely based on my own efforts and struggles to achieve my ideal goal! "[Effort]" and "[struggle]" are, of course, my only way out. If readers have other "[ways out]," we very much hope that they will be put forward. On the one hand, it can complete the intention of this humble work of throwing a brick to attract jade, and on the other hand, it can also point out the way for many young people who are trapped in depression!

The Origin of Rumors 300

— Xian

Every teacher in the school has a nickname, as common as writing "Do not urinate outside the urinal" in the toilet. The English teacher, Dr. Zhu, was introduced by the principal as having just returned from the United States. He also has a handsome face and has changed six suits in just one week since coming to the school. (Note: Sunday is a holiday.)

"[Gigolo]" is inextricably linked to the three words Dr. Zhu.

One day.

Dr. Zhu was writing American-style English on the blackboard behind the students' backs. I don't know if he wanted to show off his English scholarship, but he wrote a little too fast? The powder ash on the blackboard blew into the doctor's eyes. He was afraid that the students would unleash their college temperament and have a burst of laughter, so he hurriedly reached into his suit pocket to touch his imported silk handkerchief. As the saying goes, there is no coincidence without a book. He touched several pockets in a row, but they were all empty. The doctor squinted one eye, that embarrassed state, the white face also reflected a blush. What was even more coincidental was that Queen Lu noticed his attitude in particular, and she couldn't help but smile slightly knowingly. Dr. Zhu, in order to force himself to calm down, also reluctantly smiled slightly, thinking he was concealing it. After class.

"[The Queen and the Gigolo are flirting with each other!]"

"[Go look in the mirror!]"

One day.

It was already 5:00 p.m. Queen Lu and her cousin were walking in the campus. Many big-footed pants who thought they were qualified to be emperors also leisurely walked in the campus on the surface. The Queen's eyes were quick, and she suddenly saw Dr. Zhu coming out of the principal's office. That hurried posture reminded Miss Lu of the embarrassing scene of the powder ash flying into his eyes. She secretly told her cousin, and pointed to Dr. Zhu who was approaching. Probably all women are good at laughing, and the cousin actually chuckled. So our Queen couldn't help but smile slightly. Dr. Zhu happened to have walked in front of them, and he also inexplicably smiled slightly, and had to smile.

At dinner time.

"[There is a good reason for the Queen and the Gigolo!]"

"[You are heartbroken!]"

Saturday

Miss Lu and her banker father brought a 1933 Citroen to see the grand hotel at Yuantai. As the car was about to drive to the front of the theater, our Queen saw Dr. Zhu waiting for someone at the door again, and that facial expression had to remind Miss Lu of the embarrassing scene of the powder ash flying into his eyes. As the car stopped in front of the door, the father and daughter had just stepped out of the car, when Dr. Zhu suddenly went nearby to buy a box of musk, and ran into Miss Lu face to face. This time, the two smiled slightly at the same time, and the big gift was added with a slight nod.

"[The Gigolo can take advantage everywhere!]"

"[Go commit suicide!]"

A Non-Severe But Important Issue 301

— Cheng Sen

Should young students smoke?

Here, the smoke I am talking about is of course not "[opium]," but "[cigarettes]."

In today's society, smoking is a very common and popular thing. Even young people who are still underage in their intellectual era regard smoking as enjoyable and relieving fatigue. Yes, cigarettes can relieve people's boredom and fatigue, but they are harmful and useless to underage young people, because the quality of the smoke contains nicotine toxins and can reduce memory. Therefore, various countries have regulations prohibiting minors from smoking. In our country's schools, banning smoking is of course very strict, but they knowingly violate it and do not regard smoking as harmful. This matter of underage smoking, although very small, but if we thoroughly consider it, its drawbacks have the following three kinds:

(1) Harmful to the body

(2) Waste of money

(3) Money outflow (except for those who smoke domestic goods)

Judging from the above three items, its consumption is also considerable. And the benefits of smoking are very small (it can be said that there are none). Not smoking is not harmful to us. At this time of national crisis, we should save money to deal with foreign enemies. Young people should not smoke, and even people who stand in society, within a certain range, turn this consumed money into something useful and donate to the volunteer army. I think if the whole country implements this together, its amount will be astonishing.

Fiction

Coal Hill 302

— Written by Ed Falkowski, Translated by Sui

One

Evening, the evening city is hazy, like an old man smoking in his sleep, purple shadows tightly reflecting the chestnut and elm trees of October, the western sunlight gradually sinking,

Along Qiaoding, Wu Ke, Huixi, and other streets, yellow lights shimmered in the great and beautiful houses. The lights shone on the pianos, candlesticks, and plates in the porcelain cabinets. The aroma of dinner wafted over. The civilized families in the city were gathered together for dinner, the sounds of knives and forks clashing, cups and basins passing, and the laughter and indistinct talk of irrelevant things that happened during the day.

The black shadow of the cold dusk only fell in the poor lanes. A kerosene lamp was placed on a table covered with oilcloth, and the smoke from the lampshade rose to the ceiling. Behind the stove hung the clothes worn in the mine, waiting to dry. The shaking of the hanging clothes filled the room with a terrible sight. These clothes were to be worn every day for work. Mud-covered boots trampled in the congealing pit mud. The feet wearing the boots walked on the muddy sleepers, all the way to the tunnel.

A rough-faced woman was cutting bread, smearing it with lard, and then adding a slice of bacon. She put the bread in a round tin can and covered it. The buzzing sound in the pot echoed. Familiar fingers opened the lid, and a cloud of water vapor as large as an umbrella was released. She scooped some coffee into the boiling water. At the same time, she thought of the dirty clothes hanging behind the stove. The moisture had disappeared. Peter could wear them to climb into the mine when the mine whistle blew the next morning.

Peter was sleeping on the bed upstairs, or rather, was fantasizing. Every day, when he came back from work, he would first complain bitterly. Life, he said painfully, was not the life of his youth. The pit was like hell. Every day he only felt tired, poor and lowly.

A suitable amount of cold water had been prepared in the bathtub, with some hot water added. Peter took off his sweat-soaked underwear. He rubbed his chest with coarse soap with both hands, and then asked Mary to rub his back for him. He rubbed his whole body with soap again, and then dug out the dirt from around his ears, nose, and lips.

The pot on the stove was playing a faint tune. In this pot, Mary arranged the day's housework — dinner. After the cabbage soup was followed by shredded meat and large bones. From this large bone, Peter sucked the marrow with all his might. He forcefully knocked the bone against the edge of the table, so that the treasured bone marrow inside would loosen.

The food after the meal was only a puff of crude smoke. Outside, only the black shadows of the houses were reflected on the street, and the black shadows of the electric poles crisscrossed in the road.

Peter yawned, knocked the pipe against the door of the stove, and said: [I'm going to take a nap, Mary.]

Every bone is aching. Wake me up in two hours. I'm really tired!] This was a daily occurrence
