Film Special

Looking Back on Those Years by Charles Farrell 303

— Zhong Qin

Eight years ago, I went to Hollywood to visit a friend of my father. My father's friend worked in the theater. When I arrived in Hollywood, he introduced me to King Vidor, who gave me a small, unnamed role. After a year and a half, I gradually rose in prominence. My first leading role was opposite Madge Bellamy in "The Air Mail."

At that time, I hadn't joined Fox yet. I had a friend who was an actor at Fox. He encouraged me to join Fox. One day, I was wearing a newsboy cap when Murray dragged me into Frank Borzage's office. Murray spoke eloquently to Borzage on my behalf, but Borzage seemed not to hear, only looking at me. Later, he asked me many questions as if examining me and then offered me a contract.

I will never forget the day Borzage put my name, Charles Farrell, below Chico's name on the cast list for "Seventh Heaven." My fate with Janet Gaynor can also be said to have begun on that day. After "Seventh Heaven," Janet and I starred in eleven films together. I know that some of them were failures. The ones I was most satisfied with were "Seventh Heaven," "Street Angel," "The First Year," "High Society Blues," and my farewell film with Janet, "Merely Mary Ann."

At Fox, I co-starred with Joan Bennett, Maureen O'Sullivan, Elissa Landi, and Janet Gaynor, among others. But as I leave Fox this time, I feel the most reluctant to part with Janet Gaynor. Saying goodbye to the others was just like parting with ordinary friends.

Leaving Fox feels like leaving a loving mother. I have many brothers and sisters there who are still very happy together, but I can no longer live that life with them.

On the day I said goodbye to Janet, after we each said "take care," I felt a pang of bitterness and almost shed tears. It's a pity the photographer wasn't there, otherwise, he would have captured it on camera. Indeed, Janet and I have filmed countless scenes together, but that scene would have been the most genuine and memorable.

Film Review

Spring Waves and Amorous Shadows in Early Spring 304

— Yan Nan

Recently, films from Germany and Russia have given us excellent impressions, causing American film merchants to panic. What we have seen can be roughly divided into two types. The first is socially descriptive films that are highly meaningful, such as "Westfront 1918" and "People on Sunday." The second is musical and dance films, such as "The Congress Dances" (everyone and every newspaper thought this was a British film, but it was actually German). The first type is beyond the reach of American films. The second type can also compete with American films. This time, the Xin Guang film "Monte Carlo Madness" belongs to this type of English musical.

Its plot is somewhat similar to several amorous histories produced by Hollywood. A queen, dissatisfied with the navy's lack of funds, learns that the captain is in Monte Carlo and follows him there. Unexpectedly, upon seeing him, she suddenly falls in love and dances with him. The captain doesn't know she's the queen. Later, the captain loses a huge sum of money and, feeling aggrieved, forces the casino to return the full amount, threatening to bombard the coast otherwise. The queen doesn't take it seriously and dismisses the captain in front of all the sailors. In shame and anger, he eventually retrieves the money to pay the sailors. He then takes another ship, intending to go to Shantou. The queen, heartbroken, chases after him by ship. The vast ocean becomes the backdrop for her pursuit, forming the ending of the film.

There is nothing particularly meaningful to be found in this play, it is simply saying that "love" is the most powerful thing in the world.

The director is very clever, adopting highly meaningful backgrounds to create a complete film. The beginnings and endings are all very quiet, leaving people with lingering feelings to explore. The visual effects are excellent, and the interior scenes are also good. The photography is continental in style, and the lighting is very appropriate. The side shots are interspersed, moving and thought-provoking. In fashionable terms, it has humor amidst the prosperity.

The actors are all unfamiliar faces to us, but the unknown often hides true heroes. Sari Maritza, who plays the queen, has surpassing grace. In terms of acting, she surpasses MacDonald. She is both noble and innocent. Hans Albers, who plays the captain, has a healthy physique that is admirable. He also has good expressions. The other supporting actors are all very good. It is a pity that there is too little singing. Sari didn't sing a single song, which is a waste of excellent music. Since it focuses on Monte Carlo, it's nothing more than the following four things: dance halls, casinos, money, and women! The extravagance and indulgence can indeed be considered the extreme of auditory and visual entertainment, but it also carries a hint of contempt for women and treating them as playthings. One flaw in the set design is that the queen's palace is too simple.

This is a purely artistic success. It evokes various complex emotions such as joy, humor, and satisfaction! Those who like to watch movies may want to see it once. It has some different and interesting flavors compared to American musicals.

Girl Crazy! Screening in Nanjing 305

— Shen

"Girl Crazy" is basically a farcical musical, devoid of plot or meaning. It is simply a very beautiful and lively work within the framework of entertainment.

What is most commendable, of course, is the gathering of so many comedic characters in one work. The masterminds behind the farce are Wheeler and Woolsey. One plays a [missing text], and the other plays a lecherous womanizer. The mastermind behind the romance is Eddie Quillan, who transforms a wild western ranch into a decadent entertainment venue. The female group includes Dorothy Lee and the newly famous beauty Arline Judge. Of course, Wheeler and Woolsey's antics are the essence of the entire film. Their ingenious plans to avoid being hanged by the barbaric ranchers, as well as scenes of them disguising as Indian natives, are truly hilarious. Little star Mitzi Green's imitations of the gossiping Edna May Oliver, George Arliss, and six or seven other famous stars are also highly commendable.

The film features very melodic music and eight songs by George Gershwin, which are very pleasing to the ear. However, the "dance" is not as described in the advertisements, with only a few scenes.

Review of "Divorce in the Family" 306

— Ling He

"Divorce in the Family"

This film raises a serious question before us, and one that is not easily resolved at present. That's what I felt when I left the theater.

The film tells the story of an archaeologist who is loyal to his career. In order to travel the world and increase his knowledge, he has to travel all year round and abandon his wife. Later, the wife, feeling lonely, falls in love with a doctor and wants to marry him. However, her child will inevitably be taken to live with her new husband. Although the new husband is kind and happy to accept the child, the child does not want to lose the love of his biological father and live with a stranger. In the end, the child is taken care of by his stepfather in a situation that cannot be resolved. Regarding this, we have received much practical evidence from the minds of many children who marry with their mothers or are abused by their stepmothers. Although the play raises these questions, it does not reach a conclusion. However, perhaps this problem cannot be solved by realistic society? Unless the economic foundation has undergone a thorough transformation.

Precisely because it captures this complex subject matter, precisely because the actions of the characters in the play cannot be criticized or cursed (of course, this refers to those who are not wearing bifocals), the director of this play has indeed undertaken an extraordinary and very strenuous task. Of course, he must focus on the depiction of the child, but he cannot slack off on the other characters. In that case, the director of this film is very successful in these aspects, but it cannot be said to be perfect. At least his depiction of the father is still not sufficient.

As mentioned above, the several important actors in this play are very strenuous. In particular, that child, truly, only Jackie Cooper can do it. We are indeed worthy of respect for this outstanding little star. Louis Stone, who plays the father, has demonstrated his skills in many situations. He is even more suitable for the role in this film. As for Conrad Nagel, who plays the mother, although he is not unsuccessful, he is still inferior to the two above.

As for the other sets, lighting, sound, etc., they did not disappoint us, but there were no particularly amazing techniques either.

Overall, this is a rare film from MGM. In terms of its subject matter, it is very worthy of our attention.

Jackie Cooper's performance in "Divorce in the Family"

Bebe Daniels Suffers Greatly from a Madman 307

— Yi Yi

For nearly two years, Bebe Daniels has been relentlessly harassed by a crazed veteran named Albert Holland. He claims that Bebe is his former wife and insists that she return to the four sons she abandoned years ago.

His absurd claim that Bebe married him early on is known to everyone. Two years ago, Bebe received many love letters, but she did not pay attention to them because every famous star in Hollywood often encounters such things. So Holland stayed up all night at her house. Almost every night he waited in the courtyard of her Santa Monica seaside villa, waiting for an opportunity to renew his request. He knows everything about Bebe's movements. Even when Bebe goes to other cities, he knows, although Bebe's actions are very secretive, and no one knows except her family, but Holland always follows.

Later, Holland was arrested, and he accepted Bebe's advice and agreed to leave Hollywood, but he soon returned. Bebe's husband, Ben Lyon, listened to his friend's advice and sent him to a nursing home, but he escaped not long after.

In December 1931, Bebe and Ben petitioned the court to try Holland to prove his insanity. During the interrogation, the veteran looked very pitiful, so the merciful judge sentenced him to life in the Agnew State Hospital. But recently he came to Hollywood again, no one knows how he escaped. He once wrote to Bebe, mentioning his persecution, fearing that his wounded heart would make him take revenge. Therefore, there are bodyguards at the house in Santa Monica, and the police are strictly tracking Holland's whereabouts. Bebe and Ben agree that Holland's actions are controlled by abnormal psychology and are not deeply blameworthy, but they deeply hope that he will be arrested and that he will not be able to come out again, that this time is the last time.

Film Novel

Walking Down Broadway (10) 308

— Yu Qing

Not long after, a young woman ran to Roosevelt Hospital. She said to the nurse, "I want to see two people, one is Jimmy Morgan, and the other is Miss Millie Bloom. They were injured in the explosion on Forty-Seventh Street."

The nurse was very calm and slowly recited, "Morgan, Jimmy."

Her eyes looked towards one end of the large room. The young woman followed her eyes and saw Jimmy sitting on a bench. She rushed over immediately. Jimmy had also seen her and shouted, "Punchy! I thought you were in that house! I wanted to save you."

Punchy cried so much that her face was covered in tears, and she sobbed, "I was at Grand Central Station, sitting there waiting for the train. I was planning to go home." Later, I bought an extra edition, which was written in detail, knowing that Mona had been rescued, Millie caused the disaster by committing suicide, and you were also injured. How badly are you hurt?"

"Not badly," Jimmy said. "I'm fine, but Millie is dying."

Jimmy stood up and went with Punchy to see Millie. Millie had already been calling their names, wanting to see them. Millie was wrapped in white bandages all over, with only her eyes exposed from head to toe. Her lips were cracked, and it was extremely difficult to speak. She first asked, "Did you see the letter I left?"

After a while, she said again, "My letter was pinched in my hand, and then I opened the gas pipe. I wanted to end it all. Punchy,"

"Do you know what I told Jimmy? I have no other way to go but death."

"I don't know what you told Jimmy," Punchy said sadly. "I don't want to know either."

"But I must let you know. I love Jimmy. I heard that you were going to marry Jimmy, and my heart was broken. I felt

as if I was going crazy, so I told Jimmy many lies. But what I said was false. Later, I regretted it and went to talk to Jimmy, but Jimmy wouldn't listen to me. So I wrote him a letter and decided to commit suicide myself to clarify what is right and wrong."
